When the Enemy Breaks the Treaty: No Notice Required
Ruling that prior notice is not required when enemy breaches treaty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that attacking without notice is permissible when the enemy has breached the treaty, and identify the Prophetic evidence from the conquest of Makkah.

Core Idea
Enemy breach makes notification unnecessary; the breach itself is the notice.

In the law of war, the Hanafi school draws a clear line: if the enemy violates a peace treaty, the Muslims are not obligated to give a separate warning before attacking. This ruling is based directly on the Prophet's conduct during the conquest of Makkah, when Quraysh had already broken the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah. In this lesson, we will examine the proof texts and understand why the Hanafi school deems further notice redundant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act in question is launching a military attack against an enemy that had a treaty with Muslims. The key condition is that the enemy itself has already broken that treaty.
2
Locate the proof from Prophetic practice
The author cites the conquest of Makkah. When Quraysh violated the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah by aiding Banu Bakr against the Prophet's allies, the Prophet marched on Makkah without informing them of the abrogation.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) from Sunnah.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Two hadith are presented: one from Urwa detailing the breach, and one from Hisham showing the secrecy of the march. Both confirm that no notice of treaty termination was given.
The hadith are sahih (authentic) and serve as the basis for the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
The Hanafi position is that notification is not required after enemy breach. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that notice is still necessary. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a surprise attack is lawful.
This ikhtilaf is acknowledged in the Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Strike him in such a way that those behind him may see (2) In a hadith it is that the disbelievers of Makkah broke the treaty, so he attacked them without informing them of the treaty breach, and the conquest of Makkah occurred. They came walking until they reached Marr al-Zahran, etc.' (b) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on where the Prophet planted the flag on the day of conquest, p. 613, no. 4280, kitab al-maghazi; Sahih Muslim, chapter on conquest of Makkah, p. 102, no. 1780) From this hadith it is known that the notice of treaty breach was not given to the disbelievers of Makkah. However, they had some faint suspicion. (4) When the enemy itself broke the treaty, what benefit is there in them giving notice of treaty breach?

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi sharh tradition. The author establishes that when the enemy breaks a treaty, the Muslims may attack without prior notification. This is based on the example of the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the conquest of Makkah: the Quraysh had violated the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah by aiding Banu Bakr against Banu Ka'b, who were allies of the Prophet. The Prophet marched on Makkah without informing them of the breach. Two hadith are cited: first, the hadith of Urwa detailing the violation, and second, the hadith of Hisham showing the secrecy of the march. The author concludes that since the enemy initiated the breach, there is no need for the Muslims to give a separate notice. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that notification is only required when the Muslims themselves intend to abrogate a treaty, not when the other party has already broken it.

Key Terms
نقض العهد (naqd al-'ahd): The breaking or violation of a treaty between Muslims and non-Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Notification is always required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that an enemy's breach of a treaty renders further notice unnecessary; the breach itself is the legal justification for action.

Slaves of Disbelievers Become Free Upon Joining Muslim Army
Ruling that slaves of disbelievers become free upon joining Muslim army

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaves of disbelievers who become Muslim and reach the Muslim army, identify the hadith proof, and apply the ruling to a similar scenario.

Core Idea
A slave of a disbeliever who embraces Islam and reaches the Muslim camp is free — the Prophet declared them 'Allah's freed ones.'

In the context of jihad, the Hanafi school addresses the status of slaves belonging to enemy combatants who escape to the Muslim side. This lesson unpacks the ruling that such a slave, upon embracing Islam and arriving at the Muslim army, becomes legally free and cannot be returned. The primary evidence comes from a celebrated hadith of Ali (RA) during the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact Hanafi position: a slave of a disbeliever who becomes Muslim and comes to the Muslim army is free. Note the two conditions: embracing Islam and reaching the Muslim camp.
The ruling is classified as wajib (obligatory) — the Muslim commander must not return the slave.
2
Locate the primary proof
Identify the hadith of Ali (RA) as recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud. Focus on the context: two slaves came to the Prophet before the treaty of Hudaybiyyah, their masters demanded their return, but the Prophet refused.
The hadith is ahad in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is considered definitive (qati al-dalalah) in indicating freedom.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's strong reaction and his words 'They are the freed ones of Allah' show that the slave's freedom is granted by divine decree, regardless of their motive (whether for religion or to escape slavery). This establishes that the act of reaching the Muslim army while claiming Islam results in immediate emancipation.
The Hanafi school does not require an examination of the slave's intention — the external act suffices.
4
Cross-reference with Quranic verse
The author of the text also cites Surah al-Mumtahanah (60:10) regarding believing women emigrants. The principle that they should not be returned is extended analogically to slave men (and women) who come as Muslims.
This Quranic proof reinforces the obligation not to return the slave to the disbelievers.
5
Note the scope and differences
The ruling applies specifically in the context of jihad when the slave comes from dar al-harb. If the slave is captured during battle, different rules apply. Also, some other schools may require investigation of the slave's sincerity, but the Hanafi view follows the apparent meaning of the hadith.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school and is considered from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[2998] (19) If the slave of a disbeliever comes to the Muslim army, he is free. If a slave of disbelievers becomes Muslim and comes to the Muslim army, he will become free, he will no longer be a slave. In a hadith: From Ali, he said: 'Two slaves came to the Messenger of Allah on the day of Hudaybiyyah before the treaty. Their masters wrote to him saying, O Muhammad! By Allah, they did not come to you out of desire for your religion, but they came fleeing from slavery. It seems you will not stop until Allah sends upon you people who will strike your necks for this. And he refused to return them and said, They are Allah's freed ones. (a) O you who believe! When believing women come to you as emigrants, examine them. Allah knows best their faith. If you know them to be believers, do not return them to the disbelievers. They are not lawful for them, nor are they lawful for them.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling that any slave (male or female) belonging to disbelievers who reaches the Muslim army becomes free. The author provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) about two slaves who came to the Prophet on the day of Hudaybiyyah. The Prophet refused to return them to their masters, declaring them 'the freed ones of Allah.' This shows that even if they did not come for religious reasons, they are not to be returned. Second, the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mumtahanah, 60:10) regarding believing women emigrants, which the author interprets to include slave women: they are not to be returned to the disbelievers, implying their freedom. The author emphasizes that slavery ends upon reaching the Muslim camp. This ruling is specific to the context of jihad and dar al-harb.

Key Terms
عتقاء الله (utaqa' Allah): Those whom Allah has freed; a designation used by the Prophet for slaves who came to him from the polytheists, indicating they are free.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They must pay ransom

Key Takeaway
A slave of a disbeliever who embraces Islam and joins the Muslim army becomes free and cannot be returned, based on the Prophet's explicit declaration.

Using Captured Food and Fuel in Dar al-Harb Without Distribution
Ruling that soldiers may use captured food and fuel without formal distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using captured consumables in Dar al-Harb and apply the principle of necessity to justify immediate use without awaiting distribution.

Core Idea
In Dar al-Harb, captured food and fuel may be used immediately without distribution due to military necessity.

This lesson examines a special concession in Hanafi military fiqh: soldiers in enemy territory may consume captured food, fuel, and even use weapons without waiting for formal division of spoils. The ruling is supported by the practice of the Companions, as reported by Ibn Umar, and by the principle of necessity (darurah). Understanding this exception is important for grasping the pragmatic nature of Hanafi rulings on jihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is using captured items (food, fuel, weapons) in Dar al-Harb (enemy territory) before formal distribution.
Dar al-Harb is defined as territory under non-Muslim control where warfare is ongoing.
2
State the ruling and its level
The Hanafi school rules that such use is mubah (permissible) based on necessity.
This is a concession, not a general rule.
3
Identify the proof (dalil)
The author cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'We used to find honey and grapes in our battles and eat them without storing them (for distribution).' This is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.
The hadith demonstrates that immediate consumption was practiced by the Companions.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The permission is based on necessity (soldiers need sustenance and tools) and implicit permission from the commander. The khums and formal division are waived for urgent needs.
The principle of 'al-daruru tubuhu al-mahzurat' (necessity permits the prohibited) may also apply.
5
Note the condition of fairness
If resources are scarce, the finder should share with other soldiers to meet collective needs.
This prevents hoarding and ensures justice among the troops.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۲۹۹۹] (۲۰) اور کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کہ لشکر چارہ کھلائیں دار الحرب میں یا کھانے میں جو پائیں اس کو کھا ئیں اور ایندھن استعمال کریں۔ اور قبال کریں ایسے ہتھیار سے جو پا ئیں بغیر تقسیم کئے ہوئے۔ میدان جنگ میں کفار کی کوئی چیز ملے اور اس کو استعمال کرنے کی ضرورت ہو تو بغیر تقسیم کئے اور بغیر اس میں شمس نکالے بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔ مثلا کھا نا مل جائے تو اس کو کھا سکتا ہے۔ لکڑی ملے اس کو جلا سکتا ہے، تیل مل جائے تو استعمال کر سکتا ہے یا ہتھیار ملے تو اس سے جنگ کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ کسی چیز کی کمی ہو اور دوسرے ساتھیوں کو بھی اس کی ضرورت ہو تو پانے والا ہی سب نہ لے لے بلکہ مناسب انداز میں تقسیم کر کے لے تاکہ دوسرے ساتھیوں کی ضرورت بھی پوری ہو سکے۔ یہ ضرورت کی چیزیں ہیں اور امیر کی جانب سے ایک گونہ ان کے استعمال کی اجازت ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ گھر سے دور میدان جنگ میں ہیں اس لئے ان کے استعمال کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ہم لوگ مال غنیمت میں سے ضرورت کے مطابق استعمال کر لیا کرتے تھے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كنا نصيب في مغازينا العسل والعنب فنأكله ولا نرفعه (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما یصیب حاشیہ : (ب) حضرت ابن عمر فر ماتے ہیں کہ جنگ میں شہد اور انگور ملتا تو ہم لوگ اس کو کھاتے لیکن اٹھا کر نہیں رکھتے
[2999] (20) There is no harm in the army feeding fodder in the abode of war, and eating whatever food they find, and using fuel. And they may take as spoils any weapon they find without it being divided. In the battlefield, if something of the disbelievers is found and there is a need to use it, one may use it without division and without taking out the khums. For example, if food is found, he may eat it; if wood, he may burn it; if oil, he may use it; if weapons, he may fight with them. However, if there is a shortage and other comrades also need it, the finder should not take all for himself but should distribute appropriately so that the needs of others are also met. These are necessities, and the commander essentially permits their use because they are far from home in the battlefield, so there is no harm in using them. (2) In a hadith: we used to take from the spoils as needed. From Ibn Umar, he said: we used to find honey and grapes in our battles and eat them without storing them (for distribution). (b) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on what one gets...) Footnote: (b) Ibn Umar says that in battle, we used to find honey and grapes and eat them without storing.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility for Muslim soldiers in dar al-harb to use captured food, fuel, and weapons without waiting for formal division (qismah). The Hanafi ruling is based on necessity: soldiers in enemy territory need immediate sustenance and tools. The author mentions that such items may be used without deducting the khums (one-fifth) in the moment, but implies that proper accounting may occur later. The hadith of Ibn Umar supports this: he and others would consume honey and grapes found in battle without storing them for the official distribution. The author adds a note of fairness: if resources are scarce, soldiers should share with comrades. This permission is in effect a concession from the commander (amir). The passage reflects the pragmatic approach of the Hanafi school in military fiqh: the necessities of war allow deviation from normal rules of spoils distribution.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under the control of non-Muslims with whom Muslims are in a state of war.
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy.
خمس (khums): One-fifth of the spoils that is set aside for the state treasury (bayt al-mal) before distribution to soldiers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what did Ibn Umar and his companions do with honey and grapes they found in battle?
A) They stored them for later division
B) They ate them without storing
C) They gave them to the commander
D) They sold them

Key Takeaway
Soldiers in Dar al-Harb may use captured food, fuel, and weapons immediately due to necessity, provided they share fairly when resources are scarce.

8 min
The Fate of a New Muslim's Land and Family in Dar al-Harb
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of immovable property upon conversion in dar al-harb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the property of a harbi who converts to Islam in dar al-harb, distinguish between movable and immovable property, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).

Core Idea
A new Muslim's life and movable property are secured, but his land, wife, and adult children become fay' upon conquest.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh of siyar addresses a critical question: when a harbi (enemy combatant) embraces Islam while Muslims are conquering his territory, what becomes of his property and family? The answer depends on whether the asset is movable or immovable, and whether the person is dependent on the convert. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the status of land, with Imam Muhammad arguing for protection and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) ruling it becomes fay'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on each category
From the passage, extract the ruling for: land, wife, pregnancy, adult children, and the convert's movable property and minor children. Note that the land, wife, pregnancy, and adult children are declared fay' (spoils), while the convert's own life, movable property, and minor children are protected.
Minor children follow the legal status of their parents; adult children are independent.
2
Understand the rationale for the majority
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that land is immovable and under the sovereignty of dar al-harb, so it is not automatically secured by conversion. The wife is an independent adult in matters of faith; her status is determined by her own belief, not her husband's. Adult children are similarly independent. The pregnancy follows the mother.
The key principle: immunity for the convert's own person and property is limited to what is under his actual control and dependent on him.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's opposing view
Imam Muhammad (and Imam al-Shafi'i) holds that land should also be protected because general hadiths (e.g., 'whoever says la ilaha illallah has protected his property') are absolute, and a specific hadith (the well of Sakhr) shows that even land (a well) was returned to new Muslims.
The opposing evidence is cited from Abu Dawud and other sources; the passage quotes the well incident.
4
Study the Hanafi response and the mufta bihi
The majority responds that the general hadiths are restricted by the context of movable property or territory already under Islamic control. The well incident may be a special case or occurred before the territory was fully conquered. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that land becomes fay'.
The passage mentions that the majority view is the correct one and is followed in fatwa.

عضو کی طرح ہے۔
Muslim or dhimmi. [3002 (23)] If we conquer the abode, then his land is fay', his wife is fay', her pregnancy is fay'. There is proof in the hadith: 'Uthman ibn Abi Hazim narrated from his father from his grandfather Sakhr that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made a military expedition against Thaqif. He said: O Sakhr! When a people embrace Islam, they secure their lives and their property. So hand over to al-Mughirah his aunt. He handed her over to him. (Abu Dawud, Kitab al-Kharaj, Bab fi Iqta' al-Ardeen, vol. 2, p. 78, no. 3067?) Second hadith: Abu Hurairah ... that the Messenger of Allah said: I have been commanded to fight people until they say 'La ilaha illallah', and whoever says it has protected his property and his life from me except for a right due, and his account is with Allah. (Bukhari, Bab Wujub al-Zakat, p. 187, no. 1399; Muslim, etc.) These hadiths indicate that when one embraces Islam, his life and property become secure. Minor children follow their parents, so the ruling for them is the same as for the parents. Therefore minor children become free and are protected from killing. 'Ahraz' means secure, derived from 'hirz'. 'Wadi'ah' means something given in trust. [3002 (23)] So if we conquer their house, his land is fay', his wife is fay', her pregnancy and his adult children are fay'. Arabic: When a person becomes Muslim, his life, movable property, and minor children are protected, but his land which is in dar al-harb is not protected; rather if dar al-harb is conquered, that land becomes part of the spoils. His wife, if she is still harbiyyah, also becomes part of the spoils. The pregnancy in this woman's womb, following the mother, also becomes part of the spoils. And his adult children also remain part of the spoils; they are not protected. These people and these things are not dependent on the person who becomes Muslim, so they are not protected by his becoming Muslim. For example, land is immovable property, and though it is owned by the person who becomes Muslim, because it is dar al-harb, it is under the rule of its ruler. And that land is considered part of the land of dar al-harb, therefore it becomes spoils. Rather, Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i hold the opinion that the land would also be owned by the person who becomes Muslim and would not be counted as spoils. The hadith above states that embracing Islam secures one's property and life, and the land is also his property, so it would be protected. (2) In the hadith of Sakhr, it is mentioned that the people of al-Mughirah embraced Islam and returned the well of water, and the well is part of the land. Footnote (a): The Prophet (peace be upon him) made a military expedition against Thaqif... He said: O Sakhr! When a people embrace Islam, they secure their blood and their property. So give the people their well. He said: Yes, O Prophet of Allah. I saw the face of the Messenger of Allah change with shyness because of taking the slave girl and the well. (b) The Prophet said: I have been commanded to fight people until they say 'La ilaha illallah', and when they say it, their property and life are protected from me, except for a right due, and their account is with Allah. From this it is learned that embracing Islam also protects the land. The portion of the long hadith is: 'Uthman ibn Abi Hazim narrated... that the Messenger of Allah made a military expedition against Thaqif... O Sakhr! When a people embrace Islam, they secure their property and their blood, so give the people their water.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith mentions the well being returned, indicating that embracing Islam protects even the land in dar al-harb. (3) Hadith: Sulayman ibn Buraydah from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he used to say concerning the ahl al-dhimma: They have what they embraced Islam upon of their property, slaves, houses, land, and livestock; nothing is due upon them except charity. (Bayhaqi) This hadith indicates that a dhimmi receives his land, and by analogy a harbi would also receive his land if he embraces Islam. The wife becomes spoils because she is not dependent on her husband in matters of religion. She is a competent adult, so if she also believes, she is protected, and if she does not believe, she is a disbeliever and after capture becomes a slave girl. (2) If a Muslim man marries a Jewish or Christian woman, she is not considered Muslim because of her husband's Islam; similarly, the wife is not considered Muslim because of her husband's embrace of Islam. Therefore after conquest she becomes part of the spoils. (3) Rather, after the husband's embrace of Islam, his marriage itself is dissolved. The pregnancy of a harbiyyah woman is also fay', i.e., the child born later will be counted as spoils like property. The pregnancy is a part of the mother, so if the mother is spoils, her pregnancy is also spoils. (2) There is an athar: Sufyan said: We do not accept that; we say that if one excludes what is in her womb, she is freed entirely, for her child is like a limb of hers. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar states that the child is like a limb of the mother, so if the mother is harbiyyah, her pregnancy is also considered harbi. Adult children are not considered dependent on parents; they are themselves competent adults, so if they are harbi, they are considered harbi and not protected by the father's Islam. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet made a military expedition against Thaqif... He said: O Sakhr! When a people embrace Islam, they secure their property and their blood. So give the people their spring. He said: Yes, O Prophet of Allah. I saw the face of the Prophet change with shyness because of taking the slave girl and the spring. (b) The Prophet used to say concerning the ahl al-dhimma: Whatever property they embrace Islam upon, it all becomes theirs. Their property, slaves, houses, land, and livestock; nothing is due upon them except charity. (c) Sufyan said: We do not accept that; we say that if one excludes what is in her womb, she is freed entirely, because her child is like a limb of hers.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the Hanafi fiqh of siyar (jihad). The ruling addresses the status of a harbi (non-Muslim from dar al-harb) who accepts Islam while Muslims are conquering his territory. The core question: what property and dependents are protected by his embrace of Islam, and what becomes fay' (spoils of war)? The author clarifies that his life, movable property, and minor children are protected, but his land, his wife (if she remains harbiyyah), her unborn child, and his adult children are not; they become fay' upon conquest. The reasoning is that these are not considered dependent upon his conversion: land is immovable and remains under the rule of dar al-harb, the wife is an independent adult not bound by her husband's religion, the unborn child follows the mother, and adult children are independent. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Muhammad (and Imam al-Shafi'i) argues that land should also be protected because it is property, citing general hadiths that embracing Islam secures all property, and a specific hadith where the Prophet ordered a conquered well to be returned to new Muslims. The Hanafi response (attributed to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that these hadiths apply to movable wealth or to land that has already come under Islamic control; land still in dar al-harb is subject to the laws of war and becomes fay'. The commentary also explains the reasoning for the wife and pregnancy, and cites an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri to support that the child is part of the mother. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that the land becomes fay', consistent with the school's distinction between movable and immovable property in the context of dar al-harb.

Key Terms
فيء (fay'): Booty taken from the enemy without fighting or after conquest; in this context, property that becomes Muslim state property upon conquest.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced and war is permissible.
حربی (harbi): A non-Muslim citizen of dar al-harb with whom Muslims are at war.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living permanently under Muslim rule with a covenant of protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on the land of a harbi who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb when Muslims conquer the territory?
A) The land is protected and remains in the new Muslim's ownership.
B) The land becomes fay' (spoils) because it is immovable property under the rule of dar al-harb.
C) The land is divided equally between the new Muslim and the Muslim state.
D) The land is returned to the original non-Muslim owners.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a new Muslim's movable property is protected, but his land, wife (if harbi), and adult children become fay' upon conquest, due to their independence from the convert's faith.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Exchanging Muslim Prisoners: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prisoner exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position and the Sahibayn's position on prisoner exchange, explain each school's dalil, and evaluate the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibits prisoner exchange to eliminate fitna; Sahibayn permit it to save Muslim lives.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi disagreement over whether Muslim prisoners of war can be exchanged for non-Muslim captives. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ based on conflicting primary texts. Understanding this difference reveals how the Hanafi school balances general commands against specific precedents, and how later fatwa practice often leans towards the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: exchanging Muslim prisoners for non-Muslim captives is not permissible (haram). The enemy captives should be killed to eliminate fitna.
This is based on his interpretation of Quranic verses.
2
Identify the opposing view of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that such exchange is permissible and preferable to save Muslim lives. They are joined by Imam al-Shafi'i.
Their view prioritizes the good of rescuing Muslims.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's dalil
Abu Hanifa uses Quran 8:67 (criticizing keeping captives before subduing), 2:191 (kill polytheists wherever found), and 4:89 (seize and kill them). These command killing, not ransoming.
The verses are general and decisive for him.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil
They cite Quran 47:4 (permit ransom after capture) and hadiths where the Prophet ransomed Muslims for polytheists (e.g., from Imran ibn Husayn and Salama's father).
These specific actions seem to permit exchange.
5
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf and tarjih
Practically, if Abu Hanifa's view is followed, enemy captives are killed; if Sahibayn's view, they are exchanged for Muslim prisoners. The text does not choose, but later Hanafi fatwa often adopts the Sahibayn's position as mufta bihi.
The dispute is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُفادون بالأسارى عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى يُفادى بهم أسارى المسلمين ماكان لنبى ان يكون له اسرى حتى يثخن في الارض تريدون عرض الدنيا والله يريد الآخرة والله عزیز حکیم واقتلوهم حيث ثقفتموهم فان تولو فخذوهم واقتلوهم حيث وجدتموهم ولا تتخذوا منهم وليا ولا نصيرا فاذا لقيتم الذين كفروا فضرب الرقاب حتى اذا اثخنتموهم فشدوا الوثاق فاما منا بعد واما فداء حتى تضع الحرب اوزارها عن عمران بن حصین ان النبى فدى رجلين من المسلمين برجل من المشركين حدثنی ایاس بن سلمة حدثني ابي قال غزونا فزاره وعلينا ابو بكر فبعث بها رسول الله الى اهل مكة فقدى بها ناسا من المسلمين كانوا اسروا بمكة
And they are not to be ransomed with prisoners according to Abu Hanifa, but they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: they are ransomed with them, the Muslim prisoners. [Quran: It is not for a prophet to have captives until he has thoroughly subdued the land. You desire the goods of the world, while Allah desires the Hereafter. And kill them wherever you find them, and if they turn away, then seize them and kill them wherever you find them, and do not take from them any friend or helper. And when you meet those who disbelieve, strike their necks until you have thoroughly subdued them, then bind the captives firmly, thereafter either grace or ransom until the war lays down its burdens. And from Imran ibn Husayn that the Prophet ransomed two Muslims for one polytheist. And Iyas ibn Salama narrated from his father: We fought Fazarah with Abu Bakr... and the Prophet sent them to Mecca and ransomed with them some Muslims who had been captured there.]
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (with Imam Shafi'i agreeing with the Sahibayn) regarding exchanging Muslim prisoners for non-Muslim prisoners. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such exchange is not permissible; rather, the enemy captives should be killed to eliminate fitna. His proofs: 1) Quran 8:67 which criticizes taking captives without first subduing the land. 2) Quran 2:191 and 4:89 which command killing polytheists wherever found. Therefore, keeping captives alive and exchanging them goes against this command. The Sahibayn (and Imam Shafi'i) argue that saving Muslim lives is more important. Their proofs: 1) Quran 47:4 which permits ransom after capture. 2) Hadith where the Prophet ransomed two Muslims for one polytheist. 3) Hadith where he ransomed captured Muslims from Mecca with polytheist prisoners. The text does not explicitly choose a position, but the disagreement is recorded with evidence.

Key Terms
أسارى (asara): Plural of asir; prisoners of war.
فداء (fida'): Ransom; exchanging a prisoner for something, usually money or another prisoner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof used by Imam Abu Hanifa to prohibit prisoner exchange?
A) Hadith of the Prophet exchanging prisoners
B) The verse 'kill them wherever you find them'
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to selling weapons

Key Takeaway
While Abu Hanifa prioritized eliminating fitna over prisoner exchange, the Sahibayn offered a contrary interpretation prioritizing saving Muslim lives, illustrating the dynamic reasoning within the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Granting Favor to Captives (Al-Mann)
Inter-madhhab dispute on releasing captives without ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that releasing captives without ransom is impermissible and explain the Shafi'i counter-argument along with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Releasing a captive for free is impermissible in the Hanafi school, even if the imam perceives a maslahah.

The treatment of war captives is a critical aspect of Islamic law of war. This passage focuses on whether a Muslim ruler may release a captive without receiving any compensation (al-mann). The Hanafi school holds a strong default position of prohibition, while Imam al-Shafi'i permits it when public interest (maslahah) dictates. Let us examine the textual evidence each side brings and how the Hanafi school defends its ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: releasing a captive without ransom (al-mann) is not permissible. The text says 'la yajuz al-mann alayhim'.
2
Identify the opposing school and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i permits al-mann if maslahah exists. His evidence includes Qur'an 47:4 ('then either a favor or ransom') and two hadith: the release of eighty men of Makkah and the Prophet's comment about captives of Badr.
The Shafi'i proof relies on the literal choice in the verse and the Prophet's actions as precedents.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opposing dalil
The Hanafi school responds that the verse is contextual and the Prophet's actions were specific cases tied to particular circumstances (e.g., the Makkans had not attacked; the Badr captives were a special situation). The general principle remains prohibition to avoid weakening Muslim strength.
Hanafis argue that the general rule (amm) is prohibition unless a clear text or necessity permits otherwise.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi imam cannot release a captive without ransom even if he sees maslahah; a Shafi'i imam can if he deems it beneficial.
The disagreement affects military policy and diplomacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۰۵ (۲۶) ولا يجوز المن عليهم (۳۰۰۶ (۲۷) واذا فتح الامام بلدة عنوة فهو بالخيار ان شاء قسمها بين الغانمين وان شاء اقراهلها عليها ووضع عليهم الجزية وعلى اراضيهم الخراج.

[۳۰۰۵] (۲۶) كفار پر احسان کرنا جائز نہیں۔ بغیر کچھ لئے یوں ہی کفار کے قیدی کو رہا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہوگا۔ اوپر کی دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان قیدی کے بدلے کفار قیدی کو رہا کرنا مناسب نہیں ہے تو کچھ لئے بغیر رہا کرنا کیسے جائز ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مصلحت ہو تو کچھ لئے بغیر بھی ان کے قیدی کو چھوڑ سکتے ہیں۔ ان کی دلیل اوپر کی آیت فاما منا بعد واما فداء ( آیت ۴ ، سورۂ محمد ۴۷) ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے بعض کفار کو بغیر کچھ لئے بھی رہا کیا ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن انس ان ثمانين رجلا من اهل مكة هبطوا على النبى الله واصحابه من جبال التنعيم الذي عند صلواة الفجر ليقتلوهم فاخذهم رسول الله الا الله مسلما فاعتقهم رسول الله لا لا لها فانزل الله عز وجل وهو ا كف ايديهم عنكم وايديكم عنهم ببطن مكة الخ (الف) ( آیت ۲۴ ، سورۃ الفتح ۴۸ ) اور دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن محمد بن جبير بن مطعم عن ابيه ان النبى الله قال لاسارى بدر لو كان مطعم بن عدى حيا ثم كلمني في هؤلاء النتني لا طلقتهم له (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی المن علی الا سیر بغیر فداء، ج ۲، ص۱۰، نمبر ۲۶۸۹/۲۶۸۸ / بخاری شریف، باب ما من النبی علی الا ساری من غیران شمس ص ۴۴۳، نمبر ۳۱۳۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام مصلحت سمجھے تو بغیر فدیہ لئے بھی کفار کے قیدی کو رہا کر سکتا ہے۔
3005 (26) And it is not permissible to grant favor upon them (release without ransom). 3006 (27) And when the imam conquers a town by force, he has a choice: if he wishes, he divides it among the fighters, and if he wishes, he leaves its inhabitants upon it and imposes jizya on them and kharaj on their lands.

[3005] (26) It is not permissible to do a favor upon the disbelievers. Releasing the captive of the disbelievers for free without taking anything is not permissible. From the two hadith above, it became clear that releasing a disbeliever captive in exchange for a Muslim captive is not appropriate, so how can releasing without taking anything be permissible? Imam Shafi'i says that if there is maslahah (public interest), they can release their captive without taking anything. Their evidence is the above verse: 'then either a favor (free release) or ransom' (Surah Muhammad 47:4). (2) There is a hadith that the Prophet (saw) released some disbelievers without taking anything. The hadith is: From Anas that eighty men from the people of Makkah descended upon the Prophet (saw) and his companions from the mountains of Tan'im near the dawn prayer to kill them, so the Prophet (saw) captured them and set them free. Then Allah revealed: 'And He is the one who withheld their hands from you and your hands from them in the valley of Makkah' (Surah al-Fath 48:24). And in another narration: From Muhammad bin Jubayr bin Mut'im from his father that the Prophet (saw) said to the captives of Badr: 'If Mut'im bin 'Adi were alive and then spoke to me about these captives, I would have released them for him.' (Abu Dawood, Hadith 2689/2688; Bukhari, Hadith 3139). From this hadith, it is known that if the imam considers it to be in the public interest, he can release the disbeliever captive without ransom.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on the permissibility of releasing captives of war without any compensation. The Hanafi position is that releasing a captive without taking something in return (either ransom or a favor) is not permissible. This is based on the principle that the imam must not weaken the Muslims or strengthen the enemy by gratuitous release. The author cites two hadith from earlier in the text (not fully reproduced here) that show that releasing a Muslim captive in exchange for a disbeliever captive is appropriate, but releasing a disbeliever for free is not. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it is allowed if there is a maslahah (public interest), and he adduces two proofs: first, the Qur'anic verse (Surah Muhammad 47:4) which gives the choice between 'a favor' (mann) and 'ransom' (fida'); second, the hadith of the Prophet releasing eighty men of Makkah who intended to attack him, and the hadith of the captives of Badr where the Prophet expressed willingness to release them for Mut'im bin 'Adi. The Hanafi response to these proofs is that these cases are specific and not general; the Prophet's actions were based on particular circumstances (e.g., the people of Makkah had not attacked, and the captives of Badr were released with conditions or later developments). The Hanafi school holds that the general rule is prohibition unless there is a clear benefit that outweighs the harm, and even then it is not unrestricted. The relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the prohibition of outright gratuitous release.

Key Terms
المن (al-mann): Here, it means releasing a captive of war without taking any compensation (favor/gratuitous release).
المصلحة (al-maslahah): Public interest or benefit that would make an otherwise impermissible action permissible.
الفداء (al-fida'): Ransom paid to release a captive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on releasing a captive of war without any ransom or exchange?
A) Permissible if there is maslahah
B) Not permissible at all
C) Permissible only if the captive is a relative
D) Permissible only if the imam swears an oath

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, releasing a captive without ransom is prohibited as a general rule, while the Shafi'i school permits it if maslahah exists.

The Imam's Discretion in Distributing Conquered Lands
The author presents the imam's options with Quranic and prophetic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the imam when conquering a town by force and identify the evidence supporting each option from the Quran, Sunnah, and practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
The imam may either divide conquered land as booty or leave it with inhabitants, imposing jizya and kharaj, based on maslahah.

When a Muslim army conquers a town by force, what happens to the land? The Hanafi school holds that the imam has full discretion: he can distribute the land among the fighters or leave it with the original inhabitants and impose a land tax (kharaj) and a poll tax (jizya). This lesson examines the evidence from the Quran, the Prophet's practice at Khaybar and Makkah, and the precedent set by Caliph Umar. Understanding this ruling clarifies the flexible nature of Islamic law in matters of public interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario is conquest by force (anwa). The ruling is the imam's choice: divide among fighters or leave with jizya/kharaj.
2
Locate the primary dalil: Quran 59:7
The verse gives authority over booty to the Prophet and thus the imam, indicating discretion.
The key phrase is 'ما افاء الله على رسوله'.
3
Examine the Prophet's practice at Khaybar
Hadith show the Prophet divided Khaybar's land but also allowed Jews to work on half-share, demonstrating both options.
Sahih al-Bukhari and Abu Dawood are cited.
4
Examine the Prophet's practice at Makkah
Makkah was conquered by force but the land was not divided; inhabitants were left, showing the second option.
5
Consider the practice of Umar in Iraq
Umar left conquered Iraqi land with inhabitants and imposed kharaj, confirming the second option is valid.
This is a practice of a Rightly Guided Caliph.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲۷) اگر امام کس شہر کو طاقت سے فتح کرے تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے اسکو غازیوں کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے اور چاہے تو اس کے رہنے والے کو اس پر برقرار رکھے اور ان پر جزیہ مقرر کر دے اور اس کی زمین پر خراج مقرر القربى واليتامى والمساكين وابن السبيل كي لا يكون دولة بين الاغنياء منكم وما اتاكم الرسول فخذوه وما نهاكم عنه فانتهوا (الف) ( آیت ۷ سورۃ الحشر ۵۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جو مال غنیمت آیا وہ اللہ اور رسول کا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی جگہ جوامیر ہے اس کو تقسیم کرنے اور نہ کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ خیبر کی زمین طاقت سے فتح کی اور اس کو چھتیں حصوں میں تقسیم فرمایا۔ اور پھر یہودوں کو ہی کام کرنے کے لئے مقرر فرمایا۔ اور مکہ مکرمہ کوبھی طاقت سے فتح کیا لیکن اس کی زمین کو مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم نہیں فرمایا بلکہ وہاں کے لوگوں کو اس پر برقرار رکھا۔ بعد میں وہ لوگ ایمان لے آئے ۔ خیبر کی زمین طاقت سے فتح کی گئی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان النبي الله قاتل اهل خيبر فغلب على الارض والنخل والجاهم الى قصر ھم (ب ) اور اس زمین کو مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم کی اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن سهل بن ابي حشمة اس کو تقسیم کیا اٹھارہ حصوں پر (د) عبد اللہ بن عمر فر ماتے ہیں کہ جب خیبر فتح ہو گیا تو یہودیوں نے حضور سے کہا کہ ان کو وہیں بحال رکھا جائے اس شرط پر کہ وہ آدھی بٹائی پر کام کریں گے۔ آپ نے فرمایا جب تک چاہوں گا خیبر پر بحال رکھوں گا (ہ) حضرت عمر نے عثمان بن حنیف کو بھیجا۔ انہوں نے عراق کی پیمائش کی اور آباد اور غیر آباد جس میں پانی پہنچتا ہو ایک جریب پر ایک قیز یا ایک درہم (و) آپ نے خالد بن ولید گوا کیدر دومہ کی طرف روانہ کیا۔ پس انہوں نے اس کو پکڑ کر لایا تو اس کے خون کو معاف کر دیا اور جزیہ پر صلح کی۔
3006 (27) And when the imam conquers a town by force, he has a choice: if he wishes, he divides it among the fighters, and if he wishes, he leaves its inhabitants upon it and imposes jizya on them and kharaj on their lands.

(27) If the imam conquers a town by force, he has a choice: either he divides it among the warriors, or he leaves its inhabitants upon it and imposes jizya on them as dhimmis and kharaj on their lands. Commentary: The verse indicates that the imam has this choice: 'What Allah gave as booty to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and the Messenger and for the near relatives, orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer, so that it will not be a circulating wealth among your rich. And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, abstain from.' (Surah al-Hashr 59:7). In this verse, whatever booty came is for Allah and His Messenger, so the imam has the choice to divide or not. (2) Hadith: The Prophet conquered Khaybar by force and divided it into two halves: one half for his own emergencies and needs, and the other half for the Muslims, dividing it among them into eighteen shares. He also let the Jews work on it on half-share basis. And he conquered Makkah by force but did not divide its land among the warriors, rather left its people on it; later they embraced Islam. Evidence from Ibn Umar: The Prophet fought the people of Khaybar and conquered the land and date palms. Evidence from Sahl ibn Abi Hathma: The Prophet divided Khaybar into two halves... Evidence from Abdullah ibn Umar: When Khaybar was conquered, the Jews asked the Prophet to let them stay and work on half the produce, and he agreed. These hadith prove all three points. The evidence for leaving the inhabitants and imposing kharaj is the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab who sent Uthman ibn Hunayf to survey the Sawad (Iraq) and imposed on every cultivated irrigated acre a qafiz and a dirham. From this it is known that the inhabitants can be kept and kharaj imposed. Also the hadith: The Prophet sent Khalid ibn al-Walid to Ukaydir of Dumah, who captured him and brought him, and the Prophet spared his blood and made a treaty for jizya. This also shows jizya can be taken. Makkah was conquered by force, evidence from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet undertook the Conquest (of Makkah) in Ramadan.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that the imam has two options when he conquers a town by force (anwa): either he distributes the land as booty among the fighters (ghanimin), or he leaves the land with its original inhabitants and imposes jizya on them (as dhimmis) and kharaj on their lands. The author provides substantial evidence from the Quran, Sunnah, and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Hashr 59:7) gives authority over booty to the Prophet and thus the imam. The Prophet's actions at Khaybar show both options: Khaybar was conquered by force and its land was divided among the fighters, yet the Jews were permitted to work on it under a sharecropping arrangement. In contrast, Makkah was also conquered by force but the land was not divided; the inhabitants were left. The practice of Umar (RA) in Iraq is cited for leaving land with inhabitants and imposing kharaj. The author concludes that all three actions (division, leaving with jizya/kharaj) are established by evidence. The Hanafi position is that the imam has full discretion based on maslahah (public interest). This is the relied-upon opinion.

Key Terms
عنوة (anwa): Conquest by force, i.e., a town taken by military conquest without a peace treaty.
الجزية (al-jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslim dhimmis in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on agricultural lands of conquered territories that remain in the hands of non-Muslims or even Muslims in some cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two options the imam has when conquering a town by force according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) Kill all inhabitants or enslave them
B) Divide the land among the fighters or leave it with inhabitants imposing jizya and kharaj
C) Impose a tribute or leave the land fallow
D) Convert the inhabitants or expel them

Key Takeaway
The imam may either distribute conquered land as booty or leave it with inhabitants under jizya and kharaj, a discretion rooted in the Quran, Sunnah, and Caliphal practice.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Ruling on Enemy Livestock: Slaughter and Burn, Not Mutilate
Explains ruling on enemy livestock and prohibition of mutilation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on enemy livestock captured in war, explain the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Slaughter and burn enemy livestock to deny benefit, but never maim or burn alive — mutilation is strictly prohibited.

In jihad, the Hanafi school permits destroying enemy property to weaken them, but with strict limits against cruelty. This passage addresses the specific case of enemy livestock: must they be left, killed, or destroyed? The author rules that they must be slaughtered and their flesh burned or buried to prevent the enemy from benefiting, while any form of mutilation or burning alive is forbidden. The ruling is supported by the Quranic verse on cutting palm trees and the Prophet's practice of burning the orchards of Banu Nadir, and is distinguished from a weaker Shafi'i opinion based on a directive of Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is handling enemy livestock captured upon entering Dar al-Islam. The ruling is wajib: slaughter the animal and burn or bury its flesh. It is prohibited to leave it alive (so the enemy can recover it) or to maim it (cutting limbs while alive).
The term 'ya'qiru' (maiming) is explicitly forbidden.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The author cites Quran 59:5 (cutting or leaving palm trees is by Allah's permission to disgrace the disbelievers). This is analogically extended to livestock. Also, the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet burned and cut the palm trees of Banu Nadir (Bukhari, Muslim) shows the permissibility of destroying enemy property.
The verse is dalil on destruction of property; the hadith shows prophetic practice.
3
Analyse the analogy (qiyas) and the prohibition of mutilation
Just as trees are cut to harm the enemy, livestock are slaughtered and destroyed for the same purpose. However, the hadith of Ibn Abbas ('Do not take anything that has a soul as a target') prohibits mutilation or burning alive. Therefore, the animals must be slaughtered first (painless when done correctly) before burning the carcass.
This distinguishes between permissible destruction of property and forbidden cruelty.
4
Note the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues from the effect of Abu Bakr: 'Do not slaughter a camel or a cow except for food' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). He concludes that livestock should be left alive, not slaughtered. The Hanafi response: that directive is specific to food; here the purpose is to prevent enemy benefit, and the general proofs (Quran and Prophetic sunnah) take precedence.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi says slaughter and burn; Shafi'i says leave alive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary adopts the Hanafi position as the operative ruling (mufta bihi). The proofs from Quran and mutawatir-in-meaning sunnah are stronger than the isolated effect of Abu Bakr, which is context-specific.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin; cross-madhhab status: mukhtalaf fih.

(ه) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب تحریم قتل ماله روح الابان یذبح فیوکل، ج تاسع ، ص ۱۴۷، نمبر ۱۸۱۳۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذبح کر کے اس کو جلائے بغیر ذبیح کئے نہ جلائے۔ کیونکہ فرمایا کہ ہاتھ اور ٹانگ کاٹ کر چھوڑ دینا اچھا نہیں ہے۔ نده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ذبیح بھی نہ کرے بلکہ بغیر ذبح کئے ہوئے چھوڑ دے۔ او پراثر گزرا که لا تذبحوا بعيرا ولا بقرا الا لماكل (سن الیقی، نمبر ۱۸۱۳۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف کھانے کے لئے ذبح کرے یوں ذبح نہ کرے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب کی مویشی کو ذبح نہ کرے یوں ہی چھوڑ دے۔ حاشیه : (الف) کوئی تر و تاز و درخت کاٹو یا اس کی جڑوں پر چھوڑ دو تو یہ اللہ کے حکم سے کرو تا کہ سفیان کو روانہ کیا۔ نصیحت کی باغون کو ڈ یو نا نہیں، اس کو جلانا نہیں، چوپائے کا پاؤں نہیں کاٹنا اور نہ پھل دار درختوں کو کاٹنا (ہ) حضرت ابو بکر نے یزید بن ابو سفیان کو شام کی طرف روانہ کیا تو ان کے ساتھ کچھ دیر تک چلے۔ حدیث کا ذکر کرتے ہوئے یہ بھی فرمایا اونٹ اور گائے کو ذبح نہ کرنا مگر کھانے کے لئے۔
And upon entering Dar al-Islam, slaughter and burn it, and do not maim it, and do not leave it. Do not leave it for the benefit of the enemy, but rather slaughter it and burn its flesh so that the harbi cannot derive benefit from it. Deny the disbelievers benefit. Its proof is this verse: 'Whatever palm trees you cut down or left standing on their roots, it was by Allah's permission and so that He might disgrace the defiantly disobedient' (Surah al-Hashr 59:5). This verse says: leave the disbelievers' trees or cut them down; this is by Allah's command and the main objective is to disgrace the disbelievers. (2) From Ibn Umar: He said, 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, burned and cut down the date palms of Banu Nadir, and they were al-Buwairah' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith says: to compel the disbelievers, the trees of Banu Nadir were burned and felled. Similarly, their livestock should not be left usable. But burning it alive is not permissible; therefore, slaughter and then burn its flesh or bury it so that no benefit can be derived. A hadith states: From Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: Do not take anything that has a soul as a target' (Muslim). This hadith means: an animal should not be killed piece by piece. From this, it is understood that it should not be burned alive nor should its legs or hands be cut off and left, because that would cause pain to the animal. However, slaughter is permissible, and after slaughter, burning the flesh does not cause pain. (2) The effect is that one should not cut off the animal's limbs and leave it; that is tampering with the corpse and is impermissible. The effect is: When Abu Bakr sent troops towards Sham under Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan... 'Do not drown a palm tree, do not burn it, do not maim a beast, nor a fruit-bearing tree' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Another narration: 'Abu Bakr sent Yazid ibn Abi Sufyan to Sham, and he walked with him... and he said: Do not slaughter a camel or a cow except for food' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this effect, it is understood that it should be slaughtered and then burned, not left unslaughtered. Because he said: cutting off limbs and leaving is not good. Then Imam Shafi'i says: Do not slaughter it, but leave it unslaughtered. And there passed the effect: 'Do not slaughter a camel or a cow except for food' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this effect, it is understood that slaughter is only for food, not for this purpose. Hence, the livestock of Dar al-Harb should not be slaughtered; leave it as is. Marginal notes: (a) 'Whatever fresh tree you cut or leave on its roots, you do so by Allah's command so that the rebellious may be disgraced.' (b) The Prophet burned and cut the gardens of Banu Nadir, which was called al-Buwairah. (c) The Prophet said: 'Do not make anything that has a soul a target.' (d) When Abu Bakr sent the army towards Sham under Yazid ibn Sufyan, he advised: Do not drown gardens, do not burn them, do not maim cattle, and do not cut fruit-bearing trees. (e) Abu Bakr sent Yazid ibn Abu Sufyan to Sham and walked with him a while; mentioning the hadith, he also said: Do not slaughter a camel or a cow except for food.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling on the treatment of enemy livestock during military expeditions. It begins by stating the rule: upon entering Dar al-Islam (i.e., after capturing the animals), the livestock must be slaughtered and their flesh burned, and they must not be maimed or left alive. The reasoning is to prevent the enemy from benefiting from them. The author provides three proofs: first, the Quranic verse (59:5) regarding cutting or leaving palm trees, which is analogically applied to livestock as a means of disgracing the enemy. Second, the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet burned and cut the palm trees of Banu Nadir, indicating that destroying enemy property to weaken them is permitted. Third, the hadith of Ibn Abbas prohibiting taking any living creature as a target, which is interpreted as a prohibition of mutilating animals while alive. Thus, the Hanafi position is to slaughter the animal first, then burn or bury the flesh to deny benefit, but never to burn alive or cut limbs (tampering with the corpse). The author then addresses the opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that the animal should not be slaughtered at all but left alive, citing the effect of Abu Bakr that slaughter is only for food. The Hanafi response is that the effect is specific to food, whereas in this context, the purpose is to prevent benefit to the enemy, so slaughter and destruction are permitted. The marginal notes clarify the proofs and the historical incidents. The overall ruling is established by Quranic analogy and Prophetic practice, with a clear distinction between permissible destruction of property and impermissible cruelty to living beings.

Key Terms
يَعْقِرُ (ya'qiru): To maim or wound an animal by cutting its legs or limbs while alive
مَثْلَة (muthlah): Mutilation of a dead body or living being, e.g., cutting off limbs or ears
حَرْبِيّ (harbi): An inhabitant of Dar al-Harb (enemy territory) with whom Muslims are at war

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must be done with enemy livestock captured during war upon entering Dar al-Islam?
A) Leave them alive to be used by Muslims
B) Slaughter and burn or bury the flesh to deny benefit
C) Maim them by cutting off their limbs
D) Set them free

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires enemy livestock to be slaughtered and destroyed to prevent enemy benefit, while prohibiting any form of mutilation or burning alive.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate

Dividing Booty in Dar al-Harb: The Hanafi Position
States the ruling on postponing division of booty until it is moved to Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing booty in Dar al-Harb, explain the wisdom behind it, and evaluate the dispute with Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Booty is not fully owned until it is safe — division must wait until Dar al-Islam.

In this passage from al-Sharh al-Samari, the author explains the Hanafi position on when war booty (ghanimah) can be divided. The primary ruling is that division should be postponed until the booty is moved to Dar al-Islam, based on practical wisdom and prophetic practice. However, there is an intra-Hanafi difference with Imam Muhammad, who allows division in certain secure areas, and a parallel view held by Imam al-Shafi'i. The passage guides us through the evidence and the reasoning for the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the ruling being discussed? The act is dividing booty in Dar al-Harb. The ruling is that it should not be done until the booty is brought to Dar al-Islam.
The ruling is not absolute prohibition but a strong recommendation to delay.
2
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The author provides two reasons: (1) risk of enemy recapture means the booty is not yet fully owned; (2) after division, individual soldiers become preoccupied with protecting their share, reducing combat readiness.
These reasons are derived from maslahah (public interest).
3
Locate the exception
If the conquered territory has become secure (like Dar al-Islam) and there is no hope of counterattack, division is permissible there. This is based on the principle that the underlying 'illah (cause) – risk – no longer applies.
The exception is not a separate ruling but an application of the same principle.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The passage cites three hadith: (1) Division of Hunain booty at Ji'ranah (after Makkah became Dar al-Islam). (2) Division of Khaybar booty after the Jews were subdued. (3) Banu Qurayza (used by opponents). The Hanafi view uses the first two to show the preferred practice; the third is answered by noting that Banu Qurayza territory was also effectively secure.
All hadith are ahad, so their dalalah is zanni, but combined they support the Hanafi position.
5
Note the dispute
Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that division in Dar al-Harb is generally permissible, citing Banu Qurayza. The Hanafi response is that the Banu Qurayza incident occurred after the area was secure, so it falls under the exception.
The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the majority Hanafi view of delay, but the permissive view is acknowledged.

[۳۰۱۰ (۳۱) ولا يقسم غنيمة فى دار الحرب حتى يُخرجها الى دار الاسلام. يعقر : عقر سے مشتق ہے، کو سچ کا شنا یعنی پاؤں پر تلوار مار کر اس کو کاٹ دینا، مواش : جانور، ماشیۃ کی جمع ہے۔ [۳۰۱۰ (۳۱) دار الحرب میں غنیمت تقسیم نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ اس کو دارالاسلام تک نکال لائے۔ مال غنیمت کو دارالحرب سے دار الاسلام میں لائے تب اس کو تقسیم کرے اس سے پہلے تقسیم نہ کرے۔ دارالحرب کے اندر جب تک مال غنیمت ہے تو اس بات کا خطرہ ہے کہ کفار دوبارہ حملہ کر کے اس مال کو واپس لے لیں، چونکہ خطرہ ہے اس لئے مال مکمل طور پر مسلمانوں کا ہوا ہی نہیں۔ اس لئے اس کو مجاہدین کے درمیان ابھی تقسیم نہ کرے۔ دوسری حکمت یہ ہے کہ تقسیم ہونے کے بعد مجاہد اس کا مالک ہوگا اس لئے اس کی حفاظت میں لگا رہے گا۔ اور اچانک کوئی جنگ ہوئی تو اس میں تن من دھن سے شریک نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ کیونکہ مال کی حفاظت میں اس کا دل لگا رہے گا ۔ اور اگر مال مجموعی طور پر رہے گا تو کچھ جماعت اس کی حفاظت کرے گی اور باقی لوگ جنگ میں کود پڑیں گے۔ اس لئے دار الحرب میں مال غنیمت تقسیم نہ کرے۔ ہاں ! اگر فتح کر کے دارالاسلام کے درجے میں لا چکا ہو اور دوبارہ کفار کے حملے کر نیکی امید نہ ہو تو چونکہ دارالاسلام کے درجے میں ہو گیا اس لئے وہاں مال غنیمت تقسیم کر سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ ان انسا اخبره قال اعتمر النبي الله من الجعرانة حيث قسم غنائم حنين (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من قسم الغنيمة في غزوه و سفره ص ۴۳۱، نمبر ۳۰۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنگ حنین کی غنیمت جعرانہ میں تقسیم کی گئی اور جعرانہ مکہ مکرمہ سے قریب ہے۔ اور مکہ مکرمہ اس وقت دار الاسلام بن چکا تھا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال غنیمت دار الاسلام میں تقسیم کرے(۲) خیبر میں جو مال تقسیم کیا وہ اس لئے کہ خیبر فتح کرنے کے بعد وہ دار الاسلام کے درجے میں ہو چکا تھا۔ اور دوبارہ یہودیوں کی جانب سے حملے کا خطرہ نہیں تھا۔ عبارت یوں ہے۔ عن ابن عمران النبى الله قاتل اهل خيبر فغلب على الارض والنخل والجاهم الى قصرهم(ب)(ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما جاء فی حکم ارض خیبر ، ج ۲، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۰۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہودیوں کو اتنا مجبور کیا کہ وہ اپنے محل میں بند رہنے پر مجبور ہو گئے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ دارالاسلام کے قریب ہو چکا تھا۔ اس لئے وہاں غنیمت تقسیم کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ نان امام محمد : کی رائے یہ ہے کہ دارالحرب میں تقسیم کرنا جائز تو ہے لیکن مذکورہ وجوہ کی وجہ سے بہتر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ بنو قریظہ کے مال اور عورتوں کو تقسیم کیا۔ عن ابن عمر ان يهود النضير وقريظة حاربوا رسول الله ... فقتل رجالهم وقسم نساء هم واموالهم واولادهم بين المسلمين (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی خبر الغیر جس ۲۷، نمبر ۳۰۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ان کے مال اور اولاد اور عورتوں کو مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے۔ یہی رائے امام شافعی کی ہے۔ صلى الله عليه حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جعرانہ سے عمرہ فرمایا جہاں حنین کی غنیمت تقسیم فرمائی (ب) آپ نے اہل خیبر سے جنگ کی ۔ پس زمین اور باغات پر قبضہ کیا اور ان کو قلعے میں بیٹھنے پر مجبور کیا (ج) قبیلہ نفسی اور قریہ سے حضور نے جنگ کی۔ پس ان کے مردوں کو قتل کیا اور ان کی عورتوں ، مال اور اولاد کو مسلمانوں میں تقسیم فرمائی
[3010 (31)] And do not divide booty in Dar al-Harb until you bring it out to Dar al-Islam. يَعْقِرُ: derived from 'aqr, meaning cutting with a sword on the leg; مَوَاشٍ: animals, plural of ماشية. [3010 (31)] Do not divide booty in Dar al-Harb until you bring it to Dar al-Islam. Bring the booty from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, then divide it; do not divide it before. As long as the booty is inside Dar al-Harb, there is a risk that the disbelievers may attack again and take it back; because of this risk, the property does not fully belong to Muslims. Therefore, do not divide it among the mujahideen yet. A second wisdom is that after division, each mujahid becomes owner, so he will be preoccupied with protecting his share, and if a sudden battle occurs, he will not participate wholeheartedly because his heart is attached to protecting his property. If the booty remains collectively, then a group will guard it while the rest engage in battle. Hence, do not divide booty in Dar al-Harb. Yes, if after conquest it has become like Dar al-Islam and there is no hope of the disbelievers counterattacking, then since it has become like Dar al-Islam, he may divide the booty there. (2) There is indication of this in a hadith: 'Anas informed him: The Prophet performed Umrah from al-Ji'ranah where he divided the booty of Hunain' (Bukhari). This hadith indicates that the booty of Hunain was divided at Ji'ranah, which is near Makkah, and Makkah had become Dar al-Islam; thus, booty should be divided in Dar al-Islam. (2) The booty at Khaybar was divided because after conquering Khaybar, it had become Dar al-Islam, and there was no fear of Jewish attack. The text: 'Ibn Umar: The Prophet fought the people of Khaybar, conquered the land and palm trees, and forced them into their fortress' (Abu Dawood). This hadith shows the Jews were so subdued they were confined to their fortress, indicating it was near Dar al-Islam, so dividing booty there is no problem. Imam Muhammad's opinion: division in Dar al-Harb is permissible but not preferable due to the mentioned reasons, because a hadith states that the property and women of Banu Qurayza were divided. 'Ibn Umar: The Jews of Nadir and Qurayza fought the Messenger of Allah... so he killed their men and divided their women, property, and children among the Muslims' (Abu Dawood). This hadith shows division can be done. This is also the opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i. Marginal notes: (a) The Prophet performed Umrah from Ji'ranah where he divided the booty of Hunain. (b) The Prophet fought the people of Khaybar, conquered the land and palm trees, and forced them into their fortress. (c) The Prophet fought the tribes of Nadir and Qurayza, killed their men, and divided their women, property, and children among the Muslims.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi ruling on the division of war booty (ghanimah). The primary ruling is that booty should not be divided while still in Dar al-Harb; it must first be brought to Dar al-Islam. The reasons given are: 1) the risk of enemy recapture, meaning the booty is not yet fully under Muslim control; 2) after distribution, individual soldiers would be distracted by guarding their own shares, reducing combat effectiveness. An exception is made if the conquered territory has effectively become Dar al-Islam (no danger of recapture), in which case booty may be divided there. The author supports this with two hadith: the division at Ji'ranah (after the conquest of Makkah) and at Khaybar (after the Jews were subdued). Then Imam Muhammad's opinion is presented: division in Dar al-Harb is technically permissible, citing the precedent of Banu Qurayza, but it is not preferred due to the strategic considerations. Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with permissibility. The passage thus captures an intra-Hanafi difference and an inter-madhhab agreement on permissibility, while the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that one should avoid dividing in Dar al-Harb unless the area is secure.

Key Terms
غَنيمَة (ghanimah): Booty taken from the enemy during war, including property, women, and children
دار الحَرْب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under the control of non-Muslims with whom Muslims are in a state of war
دار الإسْلام (Dar al-Islam): Territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law prevails

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why should booty not be divided in Dar al-Harb?
A) Because it is haram to handle booty in enemy territory
B) Because of the risk of enemy recapture and distraction of fighters
C) Because the Prophet never divided booty outside Dar al-Islam
D) Because only the caliph can divide booty

Key Takeaway
Booty should be divided only after it is brought to a secure area (Dar al-Islam) to ensure full ownership and maintain military focus, though division is permissible if the area is effectively secure.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
8 min
Delaying Division of Spoils Until Dar al-Islam
States the ruling and explains wisdom and evidence for delaying division of spoils

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing spoils in enemy territory, explain the two wisdoms, and identify the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Spoils must be brought to Muslim territory before division to ensure security and collective readiness.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Book of Siyar: spoils of war (ghanimah) must not be divided while still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). The passage explains the wisdom behind this delay and provides evidence from the Sunna. You will also encounter a significant intra-Hanafi difference—Imam Muhammad's permissive view—and an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. Understanding this rule reveals how the Hanafi school prioritizes practical security and communal defense over individual ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
The passage states that the imam (commander) should not divide spoils in Dar al-Harb. The condition is that the spoils must be brought to Dar al-Islam first. Identify the act (dividing spoils) and the conditional prohibition.
The ruling is a prohibition with karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibited disliked), not absolute haram.
2
Explain the Two Wisdoms
The commentator gives two reasons: (1) risk of recapture by the enemy—spoils are not fully owned until secure; (2) if each soldier receives his share immediately, he becomes preoccupied with protecting it and may not engage in sudden counterattacks. Collective ownership keeps the army ready.
The second wisdom highlights the strategic advantage of communal responsibility during campaign.
3
Locate the Proof from the Sunnah
The passage cites the hadith of Hunayn: the Prophet divided the spoils at al-Ji'ranah, which was part of Dar al-Islam. Also the conquest of Khaibar where division occurred on site because the land had effectively become Dar al-Islam. These show that the preferred practice is to delay division until safe territory.
The proofs are dalil naqli (textual evidence) supporting the Hanafi view.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that division in Dar al-Harb is permissible (ja’iz) but makruh tanzihan (mildly disliked). His evidence is the hadith of Banu Qurayzah where the Prophet divided their wealth and families immediately after their surrender. The Hanafi response is that Banu Qurayzah's territory effectively became Dar al-Islam after surrender.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the first view—division is not allowed.
5
Recognize the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i adopts the permissive view, citing the same Banu Qurayzah hadith. The Hanafi school argues that the context of that incident (surrender) changed the status of the land. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Shafi'is may distribute spoils immediately if they deem it safe, while Hanafis wait.
This illustrates how a single hadith can be interpreted differently based on the principle of territorial status.

صلى الله
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جعرانہ سے عمرہ فرمایا جہاں حنین کی غنیمت تقسیم فرمائی (ب) آپ نے اہل خیبر سے جنگ کی ۔ پس زمین اور باغات پر قبضہ کیا اور ان کو
قلعے میں بیٹھنے پر مجبور کیا (ج) قبیلہ نفسی اور قریہ سے حضور نے جنگ کی۔ پس ان کے مردوں کو قتل کیا اور ان کی عورتوں ، مال اور اولاد کو مسلمانوں میں تقسیم فرمائی
The Book of Siyar. [Rule 31] He should not divide spoils in the abode of war until he brings them out to the abode of Islam. ... Commentary: Do not divide the spoils in Dar al-Harb until you bring them to Dar al-Islam. The risk is that the disbelievers may attack and retake the wealth; it is not fully owned by Muslims. Another wisdom is that after division, each fighter will be preoccupied with protecting his share and may not participate in sudden battles. If it remains collective, some guard it while others fight. So do not divide in Dar al-Harb. However, if the land is conquered and becomes like Dar al-Islam, division may occur there. Indication from hadith: Anas reported that the Prophet performed Umrah from al-Ji'ranah where he divided the spoils of Hunayn (Bukhari). Also, Khaibar was divided after conquest because it became Dar al-Islam. Imam Muhammad holds that division in Dar al-Harb is permissible but not preferred; he cites the division of Banu Qurayzah's spoils. This is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Siyar. The core ruling is that spoils of war (ghanimah) should not be distributed while still in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). Instead, they must be transported to Muslim territory (Dar al-Islam) before division. The commentator explains two primary wisdoms: first, the risk that disbelievers may recapture the spoils, meaning Muslims' ownership is not secure; second, if each soldier receives his share immediately, he will be occupied with protecting his property and may not be ready for sudden combat. If the spoils remain communal, a group guards them while others fight. The passage then presents exceptions: if the conquered land effectively becomes Dar al-Islam (e.g., after the conquest of Khaibar), division on the spot is allowed. It also cites a difference of opinion: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) considers division in Dar al-Harb permissible but not preferable, citing the Prophet's division of Banu Qurayzah's spoils while still in their territory. Imam al-Shafi'i takes the permissive view. Footnotes provide hadith evidence: the Prophet divided the spoils of Hunayn at al-Ji'ranah, which was close to Makkah and part of Dar al-Islam, and the conquest of Khaibar where the land came under Islamic control.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (Dar al-Harb): Territory under non-Muslim control where Islamic law is not enforced and where hostilities are possible.
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy after battle; specifically refers to movable property (e.g., weapons, money, captives), excluding land.
ردء (rad'): A helper or supporter in the army, not directly engaged in combat but providing assistance, such as guarding supplies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi position in this passage, where must spoils be taken before division?
A) To the nearest mosque
B) To Dar al-Islam
C) To the commander's tent
D) To the battlefield

Key Takeaway
Spoils must be brought to Dar al-Islam before division to ensure ownership security and collective defense readiness.

The Helper and Fighter Are Equal in Spoils
A ruling with evidence from prophetic practice and caliphal decision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a non-combatant supporter (rad') receives an equal share of spoils as a combatant, citing the primary proofs.

Core Idea
In spoils, the helper and fighter are equal – presence in the campaign, not combat role, determines share.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling in the law of jihad: the distribution of spoils. The Hanafi school holds that every member of the army, whether they fight directly or provide support, receives an equal share. This ruling, based on the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs, emphasises the collective nature of the campaign. We will explore the proofs and understand the rationale behind this equality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
State the ruling: the helper (rad') and the fighter (muqatil) are equal in entitlement to spoils. The scope includes all members of the army present for the campaign, regardless of actual combat role.
The ruling is found explicitly in the matn: 'والردء و المقاتل في العسكر سواء'.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the action of the Prophet at the Battle of Hunayn. Sayyiduna Abbas (RA) held the reins of the Prophet's mule to prevent it from bolting, while others fought. Despite not fighting, Abbas received an equal share of the spoils (Muslim).
The hadith text: 'قال عباس وانا آخذ بلجام بغلة... وقسم رسول الله غمنائمهم بين المسلمين'.
3
Examine the supporting evidence
Two additional proofs: (1) The ruling of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) after the Battle of Nihawand: Kufan reinforcements arrived after the victory but before distribution, and Umar ruled that they are entitled to a share because they were present for the battle (الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعة). (2) The hadith from Abu Dawood that the Prophet divided spoils equally among all participants, young and old, fighter and helper.
These proofs reinforce the principle that presence, not combat, is the criterion.
4
Understand the authority weight
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah with no intra-Hanafi disagreement. The evidence is considered decisive (qat'i al-dalala) and is relied upon for fatwa. The imam may use discretion for a greater benefit, but the established sunnah is equality.
The hanafi_position_box confirms: authority_weight = zahir_riwayah, cross_madhhab_status = muttafaq_alayh.
