حاشیہ : ( الف ) اہل بصرہ نے اہل نہاوند سے جنگ کی تو ان کو اہل کوفہ کے ذریعہ مددی گئی۔ اہل بصرہ کے امیر عمار بن یاسر تھے ۔ پس اہل کو نہ دشمن پر غالب ہونے کے بعد شریک ہوئے۔ پس اہل کوفہ نے غنیمت مانگی اور اہل بصرہ نے چاہا کہ اہل کوفہ کے لئے غنیمت تقسیم نہ ہو ۔ اس لئے بنی تمیم کے ایک آدمی نے حضرت عمار بن یا سر کو کہا کس لئے تم ہماری غنیمت میں ان کو شریک کرنا چاہتے ہو۔ اور حضرت عمار کا کان حضور کے ساتھ کٹ گیا تھا تو حضرت عمار نے حضرت عمر کولکھا تو حضرت عمرؓ نے جواب دیا کہ مال غنیمت اس سب کو ملے گا جو جنگ میں شریک ہوا (ب) حضرت عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضور کے ساتھ جنگ حنین میں شریک ہوا... حضرت عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضور کے خچر کی لگام پکڑے ہوئے تھا۔ اس کو روکتا تھا تا کہ خچر تیزی سے آگے نہ بڑھ جائے۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ حضور نے اس کی غنیمت مسلمانوں میں تقسیم کی۔
[Rule 32] The helper and the fighter in the army are equal. Commentary: Some fighters engage in combat while others assist; both receive equal shares in the spoils. There is evidence: Tariq ibn Shihab reported that when the people of Basra fought Nihawand, they were reinforced by people of Kufa under Ammar ibn Yasir after the victory. The Kufans asked for spoils, but the Basrans wanted to exclude them. A man from Banu Tamim said to Ammar, 'Do you want to share our spoils?' (Ammar's ear had been cut off with the Prophet). So they wrote to Umar ibn al-Khattab, and he replied: 'Spoils belong to whoever was present at the battle.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Thus, even those who join later get a share. Also, at Hunayn, Abbas (RA) held the reins of the Prophet's mule while others fought, yet he received an equal share (Muslim). Abu Dawood reports that the Prophet divided spoils equally among all, young and old, fighter and helper.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents a second ruling: that the helper (rad') and the fighter (muqatil) are equal in entitlement to spoils. The commentator explains that even if some men are engaged in direct combat while others provide support (e.g., guarding supplies, holding animals), their shares are equal. He supports this with several proofs: First, the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) in the Battle of Nihawand: reinforcements from Kufa arrived after the victory, and Umar ruled that they were entitled to a share because they were present for the battle. Second, the example of Sayyiduna Abbas (RA) at Hunayn: while he held the Prophet's mule to prevent it from bolting, other Companions fought, yet Abbas received an equal share. Third, a hadith from Abu Dawood states that the Prophet divided spoils equally among all participants, old and young, fighter and supporter. This establishes the Hanafi rule that no distinction is made between combatants and non-combatant supporters; everyone present for the campaign shares equally in the spoils, provided they are part of the army.

Key Terms
ردء (rad'): A person who provides assistance to the army without directly engaging in combat, such as guarding equipment or tending to animals.
مقاتل (muqatil): A warrior who directly fights in battle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the ruling of Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) regarding the Kufan reinforcements who arrived after the battle of Nihawand?
A) They get no share because they missed the fighting
B) They get a share equal to the fighters because they were present for the battle
C) They get a smaller share for arriving late
D) They get full share only if they fought

Key Takeaway
Presence in the campaign, not combat role, is the determining factor for spoils distribution.

Reinforcements Sharing Booty Before It Reaches Dar al-Islam
Ruling on when reinforcements joining in Dar al-Harb share in booty, with a dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when reinforcements share in booty and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, including the evidence and the practical consequence.

Core Idea
Reinforcements share booty if they join before it leaves Dar al-Harb—even after battle ends.

The question of when reinforcements are entitled to a share in the spoils of war has practical consequences for campaign planning. The Hanafi school establishes a clear condition: the booty must still be in Dar al-Harb. This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence from the Caliphs, and the contrasting view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The central act is the arrival of reinforcements (al-madad) during a campaign. Determine the exact condition the Hanafi school uses to grant them a share.
Condition: reinforcements join before the booty is taken to Dar al-Islam, not necessarily before battle ends.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
State that the Hanafi position grants them an equal share. Identify the two athars from Caliphs Umar and Abu Bakr as proof.
The first athar: Umar gave Kufans a share in Basran booty (Bayhaqi no. 17953). Second: Abu Bakr gave Ikrimah's reinforcements a share after the conquest of Najir (Bayhaqi no. 17952).
3
State the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that only those who join before the fighting ends can share. Identify his evidence: Umar's letter to Sa'd at Qadisiyyah (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah no. 33211).
The Qadisiyyah letter explicitly limits shares to those who join before the battle separates.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
Explain why the Hanafi school does not adopt the Qadisiyyah letter as a general rule. The response is that the Qadisiyyah case was specific to that situation and does not set a universal precedent.
The general practice of the Caliphs overrides the specific letter.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafi school includes late reinforcements before moving booty; Shafi'i excludes them unless they joined before the battle ended.
Consequence: In Hanafi fiqh, commanders can expect reinforcements to share even after victory, affecting incentive structures.

[۳۰۱۲ (۳۳) واذا لحقهم المدد فى دار الحرب قبل ان يُخرجوا الغنيمة الى دار الاسلام شاركوهم فيها إذا ان کو مدد لاحق ہوئی دار الحرب میں غنیمت کو دارالاسلام میں لانے سے پہلے تو وہ اس میں شریک ہوں گے۔ ایک لشکر پہلے سے دار الحرب میں جنگ کر رہا تھا۔ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد لیکن مال غنیمت تقسیم کرنے سے پہلے اور اس کو دار الاسلام تک لانے سے پہلے مجاہدین کی دوسری جماعت اس کی مدد کے لئے مل گئی تو ان کو بھی مال بعث عكرمة بن ابى جهل في خمس مائة من المسلمين مددا لزياد بن لبيد وللمهاجر بن ابى امية فوافقهم الجند قد افتتحوا النجير باليمين فاشركهم زياد بن لبيد وهو ممن شهد بدرا في الغنيمة (الف) (سن اللبیہقی ، باب الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعة ، ج تاسع ص ۸۶، نمبر ۱۷۹۵۲) اس اثر میں بھی ہے کہ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد مدد پہنچی تو اس کو بھی مال غنیمت میں حصہ دیا گیا۔ نوں پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ دارالحرب سے نکلنے سے پہلے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مال غنیمت تقسیم کرنا ٹھیک نہیں ۔ اس لئے مصنف کی عبارت میں یہ ہے کہ مال غنیمت دار الاسلام لانے سے پہلے کوئی جماعت مدد کے لئے لشکر کے ساتھ مل جائے تو ان کو حصہ ملے گا۔ ورنہ اصلی قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ مال غنیمت تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے جماعت مل جائے تو ان کو حصہ ملے گا۔ نان امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جنگ ختم ہونے کے بعد ملے تو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ كَتَبَ عُمَرُ إِلَى سَعْدٍ يَوْمَ الْقَادِسِيَّةِ: إِنِّي قَدْ بَعَثْتُ إِلَيْكَ أَهْلَ الْحِجَازِ وَأَهْلَ الشَّامِ، فَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْقِتَالَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَفَرَّقُوا فَأَسْهِمْ لَهُمْ (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۰۹ فی القوم تکیون بعد الوقعیہ پھل کھم شی ء ، ج سادس جس ۴۹۷، نمبر ۳۳۲۱۱) اس میں جنگ ختم ہونے سے پہلے شریک ہونے والے کو حصہ دلوایا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابو بکر نے حضرت عکرمہ کو پانچ سو مجاہد کے ساتھ زیاد بن لبید اور مہاجر بن امیہ کی مدد کے لئے بھیجا۔ پیشکر سے اس وقت ملے جب یمن میں نجیر کو فتح کر چکے تھے تو زیاد بن لبید نے ان کو غنیمت میں شریک فرمایا، حضرت زیاد جنگ بدر میں شریک ہوئے تھے۔ (ب) حضرت عمر نے حضرت سعد کو قادسیہ کے دن لکھا کہ میں اہل حجاز اور ہل شام کو بھیج رہا ہوں۔ ان میں سے جس نے جنگ کو قتل سے پہلے پایا ان کے لئے حصے دو
(33) And if reinforcements join them in the abode of war before they take out the booty to the abode of Islam, they share in it. If reinforcements join them in Dar al-Harb before they bring the booty to Dar al-Islam, then they will share in it. An army was already fighting in Dar al-Harb. After the battle ended but before the booty was distributed and before it was brought to Dar al-Islam, another group of mujahideen joined them for assistance, so they will also receive an equal share in the booty. Above, the judgment of Umar has passed in which he gave the people of Kufa a share in the booty of the people of Basra. That athar has passed (Sunan al-Bayhaqi no. 17953). Another athar: Abu Bakr al-Siddiq sent Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl with five hundred Muslims as reinforcements for Ziyad ibn Labid and al-Muhajir ibn Abi Umayyah. They met the army after they had opened Najir in Yemen, so Ziyad ibn Labid, who was present at Badr, gave them a share in the booty (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ghanimah li-man Shahida al-Waq'ah, vol. 9, p. 86, no. 17952). In this athar as well, reinforcements arrived after the battle was over, but they were given a share in the booty. It has passed earlier that according to Imam Abu Hanifah, it is not proper to distribute booty before leaving Dar al-Harb. Therefore, the author's wording is that if a group joins the army as reinforcements before the booty is brought to Dar al-Islam, they get a share. Otherwise, the basic rule is that if a group joins before the distribution of booty, they get a share. Imam al-Shafi'i states that if they arrive after the battle, they do not get a share in the booty. His evidence is this athar: Umar wrote to Sa'd on the day of Qadisiyyah: 'I have sent to you the people of Hijaz and the people of Sham, so whoever among them joins the fighting before they disperse, give them a share.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ... vol. 6, p. 497, no. 33211) In this, only those who joined before the battle ended are given a share. Footnote (a): Abu Bakr sent Ikrimah ibn Abi Jahl with five hundred mujahideen as reinforcements for Ziyad ibn Labid and al-Muhajir ibn Abi Umayyah. They met the army when they had conquered Najir in Yemen, so Ziyad ibn Labid gave them a share in the booty; Ziyad was present at Badr. (b) Umar wrote to Sa'd on the day of Qadisiyyah: I am sending the people of Hijaz and the people of Sham to you. Whoever among them reaches the fighting before the battle separates, give them shares.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi ruling: if reinforcements join the army in Dar al-Harb before the booty is transported to Dar al-Islam, they share in the booty equally, even if they arrive after the battle. The author supports this with the practice of Caliph Umar in the Kufa-Basra incident and the practice of Abu Bakr in the case of Ziyad ibn Labid. The Hanafi position is that the key is whether the booty has been brought to Dar al-Islam, not whether the battle is over. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that only those who join before the fighting ends are entitled, citing Umar's letter to Sa'd at Qadisiyyah. The Hanafi response, implicit in the text, is that the Qadisiyyah case is specific and does not negate the general principle established by other precedents. The condition 'before they take out the booty to Dar al-Islam' is crucial; once the booty is in Dar al-Islam, latecomers lose their right.

Key Terms
المدد (al-madad): Reinforcements sent to support an army in the field.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): The territory under non-Muslim control where hostilities are permitted.
دار الاسلام (dar al-islam): Territory under Muslim rule where Islamic law is applied.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for reinforcements to be entitled to a share in the booty?
A) They must join before the battle ends
B) They must join before the booty is taken to Dar al-Islam
C) They must join before the booty is distributed
D) They must join before the army leaves Dar al-Harb

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants reinforcements a share in booty if they join before it is taken to Dar al-Islam, based on general practice of the Caliphs, while the Shafi'i school restricts it to before the battle ends.

Market Sellers in the Army Have No Right to Booty Unless They Fight
Ruling that non-fighting traders have no booty share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on booty entitlement for non-fighting traders and explain the proof from the athar of Umar.

Core Idea
Booty belongs to those who fight, not to traders.

This lesson addresses a key issue in the fiqh of jihad: who is entitled to a share of the booty? The Hanafi school holds that mere presence in the army camp is insufficient; active participation in battle is required. This ruling is supported by the practice of the Caliph Umar ibn al-Khattab.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the explicit ruling: market sellers in the army have no right to booty unless they actually fight.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is an athar (tradition) of Umar ibn al-Khattab who wrote: 'The booty belongs to those who witnessed the battle.'
This is a mawquf hadith reported by Bayhaqi.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'shahida al-waq'ah' (witnessed the battle) implies active participation in fighting, not mere physical presence or trade.
4
Note the role of intention
The Hanafi school considers intention (niyyah): traders come to profit, not to fight, so they do not qualify.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Some other schools may interpret presence as sufficient; Hanafis restrict entitlement to actual fighters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۱۳ (۳۴) ولا حق لاهل سوق العسكر في الغنيمة الا ان لشکر کے بازار والوں کو حق نہیں ہے غنیمت میں مگر یہ کہ وہ بھی قتال کریں۔ لشکر میں شامل ہیں لیکن ان کا مقصد قتال کرنا نہیں ہے اپنی دکان لگا کر تجارت کرنا ہے تو ان کو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا۔ اثر میں ہے کہ جو لوگ جنگ میں شریک ہوں ان کو حصہ ملے گا اور یہ لوگ نیت کے اعتبار سے جنگ میں شریک نہیں ہیں۔ یہ لوگ تو اپنی تجارت بڑھانے کے لئے آئے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان کو مال غنیمت میں حصہ کیسے ملے گا؟ (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ أَنَّ الْغَنِيمَةَ لِمَنْ شَهِدَ الْوَقْعَةَ (ج) (سن الليبقى ، باب الغنيمة لمن شهد الوقعه ، ج تاسع میں ۸۶ نمبر ۱۷۹۵۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ غنیمت اس حاشیہ : (ج) حضرت عمر نے لکھا کہ (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
(34) And there is no right for the people of the army market in the booty unless they also fight. The people of the army market have no right to the booty unless they also fight. They are part of the army, but their purpose is not to fight; they set up shops and trade, so they do not receive a share in the booty. In an athar, those who participate in the battle get a share, and these people, by intention, are not participants in the battle; they came to enhance their trade. So how can they get a share? (2) In an athar, Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote: 'The booty belongs to those who witnessed the battle.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Ghanimah li-man Shahida al-Waq'ah, vol. 9, p. 86, no. 17954) In this athar, the booty is for... Footnote (c): Umar wrote that (remaining on next page).
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The ruling states that people who are part of the army but only engage in trade and do not participate in fighting have no share in the booty. The proof is the athar of Umar: 'The booty belongs to those who witnessed the battle.' The word 'witnessed' implies active participation in the fighting, not mere presence. Therefore, those who are present solely for trade do not qualify. The ruling emphasizes intention (niyyah): since their intention is trade, not jihad, they are not entitled to booty.

Key Terms
سوق العسكر (suq al-askar): The market established within or near the army for trade purposes.
شهد الوقعة (shahida al-waq'ah): To witness the battle, meaning to participate actively in the fighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT entitled to a share in the booty?
A) A soldier who fights in the battle
B) A helper who holds the reins of a horse
C) A trader who sets up a shop in the army camp
D) A reinforcement that arrives after the battle but before booty is moved to Dar al-Islam

Key Takeaway
Booty is reserved for those who actively participate in battle; traders and non-fighters have no claim.

Ruling on Spoils for Hired Workers (Ajir)
Ruling that only fighters receive spoils, with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an ajir's entitlement to ghanimah and explain the hadith proof that establishes the condition of active participation.

Core Idea
An ajir gets no spoils unless he fights—the hadith of Salama makes participation the condition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on distributing spoils to non-combatants accompanying the army, such as hired workers. The school relies on a specific hadith to assert that only those who actually fight or intend to fight are entitled. We will unpack the proof and compare it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the distribution of ghanimah. The ruling under discussion is whether an ajir (hired worker) receives a share. State the Hanafi position: no share unless he fights or intends to fight.
This is the basic ruling statement.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa', narrated by Iyas ibn Salama, found in Sahih Muslim and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba. The hadith shows Salama was an ajir and did not receive a share until after he fought.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action—withholding a share before fighting and granting it after—demonstrates that fighting is the decisive condition. The phrase 'then he gave me two shares' indicates the change in status.
The explicit contrast in the hadith is key.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i held that those present on the battlefield, even if they do not fight, may still be entitled because their presence has value. He bases this on a broader understanding of contribution.
This is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school prefers its position because the direct hadith explicitly links entitlement to fighting. The Shafi'i argument relies on analogy and general benefit, but the explicit textual proof takes precedence.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقاتلوا [۳۰۱۴ (۳۵) واذا امن رجل حر او امرأة حرَّةً كافرا او جماعة او اهل حصن او مدينة صح امـانهـم ولـم يجز لاحد من المسلمين قتلهم الا ان يكون في ذلك مفسدة کے لئے ہے جو جنگ میں شریک ہوا ہو یا جنگ میں شرکت کی نیت سے شامل ہوا ہو۔ اور یہ لوگ جنگ میں شرکت کی نیت سے شامل نہیں ہوئے ہیں اس لئے ان کو مال غنیمت میں حصہ نہیں ملے گا (۲) مسلم بن سلمہ بن اکوع کی لمبی حدیث ہے کہ وہ اجیر تھے تو حصہ نہیں دیا لیکن جب اہل مکہ سے قتال کیا تو حضور نے گھوڑے سوار کا حصہ دیا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایسے لوگوں کے قتال کرنے سے حصہ ملے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ حدثنی اياس بن سلمة حدثنى ابى ... قال كنت تبيعا لطلحة بن عبيد الله اسقى فرسه واحسه واخدمه واكل من طعامه... اس لمبی حدیث کے اخیر میں ہے ... ثم اعطاني رسول الله الا الله سهمين سهم الفارس وسهم الراجل (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب غزوة ذی قرد و غیر ها ص ۱۱۳ نمبر ۱۸۰۷ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۰۷ امن قال للعبيد والا جیر کھم، ج سادس، ص ۴۹۶، نمبر ۳۳۲۰۴) نا امام شافعی کی ایک رائے یہ ہے کہ کسی نہ کسی انداز میں یہ لوگ بھی معرکہ میں شریک ہوئے ہیں اس لئے اوپر کے اثر کی بنیاد پر ان کو بھی مال غنیمت میں حصہ ملنا چاہئے ۔ لفت اهل السوق : بازار والے، دوکاندار۔
They fight. [Section 3014 (35)] And if a free man or free woman gives aman to a kafir, or a group, or the people of a fortress, or a city, their aman is valid, and it is not permissible for any Muslim to kill them unless there is corruption in that. The meaning of this is for one who participated in war or intended to participate. And these people did not intend to participate in war, so they will not receive a share of the spoils. (2) There is a long hadith from Muslim bin Salama bin Akwa' that he was an ajir (hired worker) and was not given a share, but when he fought the people of Mecca, the Prophet gave him a horseman's share. This indicates that such people get a share if they fight, otherwise not. Narrated to me Iyas bin Salama, narrated to me my father... he said: I was a hired worker for Talha bin Ubaidullah, I watered his horse, groomed it, served him, and ate from his food... At the end of this long hadith is: ...then the Messenger of Allah gave me two shares: the share of a horseman and the share of a foot soldier. (Reference: Muslim, etc.) Imam Shafi'i has one opinion that these people also participated in the battle in some way, so based on the above athar they should also receive a share of the spoils. Lufat ahl al-suq: market people, shopkeepers.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the distribution of spoils (ghanimah) for those who do not directly fight. The Hanafi position is that only those who actively participate in battle or intend to participate receive a share. Hired workers (ajir) who do not fight do not get a share unless they actually engage in combat. The proof is the hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa', who was an ajir and only received a share after he fought. The hadith narrated by Iyas ibn Salama confirms that the Prophet gave him both a horseman's share and a foot soldier's share after he fought. A contrary opinion of Imam al-Shafi'i is mentioned, who holds that such individuals may still get a share because they were present in the battlefield in some capacity. However, the Hanafi school maintains the ruling based on the explicit hadith. The term 'lufat ahl al-suq' glosses 'market people' as shopkeepers who may also be present but not fighters.

Key Terms
اجیر (ajir): A hired worker or servant who accompanies the army but does not have the intent to fight.
سهم (sahm): A share of the spoils; specifically one portion for a foot soldier and two for a horseman.
غنیمت (ghanimah): War booty taken from the enemy after a battle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling based on the hadith of Salama, what is the condition for an ajir to receive a share of ghanimah?
A) Being present on the battlefield.
B) Being employed by a warrior.
C) Actually fighting or intending to fight.
D) Being a free Muslim.

Key Takeaway
An ajir (hired worker) does not receive a share of spoils unless he actively fights or clearly intends to fight, as proven by the hadith of Salama ibn al-Akwa'.

Ruling on Aman (Safe Conduct) by Free Muslims
Ruling that free Muslim men and women can grant aman binding on all Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who can grant aman and explain that it binds all Muslims, with the imam’s authority to annul only if corruption arises.

Core Idea
Any free Muslim's aman binds the whole community; only the imam may annul it publicly for corruption.

This passage addresses the legal framework for aman (safe conduct) in Hanafi fiqh. It establishes that both free Muslim men and women can grant aman to enemy non-Muslims, and that such aman is binding on all Muslims. The text also provides the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and explains the imam's limited authority to annul aman if public interest requires it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Aman is a grant of protection to a harbi (enemy non-Muslim). The passage rules that aman given by a free Muslim man or woman is valid and binding on all Muslims. It is wajib to honour it.
Note that the ruling covers both individuals and groups (e.g., people of a fortress or city).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites multiple proofs: the general prohibition against breaking covenants (Quran 8:56), the requirement to annul openly if treachery is feared (Quran 8:58), the hadith that the dhimma of Muslims is one (from Ali), and the specific hadith of Umm Hani proving a woman's aman is valid.
The hadith of Umm Hani is key for the ruling on women.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Quran 8:56 condemns covenant-breaking, implying aman must be upheld. Quran 8:58 permits open annulment only when treachery is feared, supporting the imam's role. The hadith of Ali shows the unity of Muslim responsibility, and Umm Hani's hadith directly shows the Prophet accepted a woman's aman.
The proof shows the ruling is derived from both primary texts and the practice of the Prophet.
4
Note the condition for annulment
If there is corruption (mafsada) in maintaining aman, the imam may annul it, but only after public announcement so the protected party is not caught unaware. This avoids treachery.
The imam's annulment is not arbitrary; it requires a clear reason and due notice.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position. The proofs are strong (muttafaq alayh) and no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded.
The ruling is practical for situations where individual Muslims face enemy combatants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امان کے احکام کے (۳۰۱۴) (۳۵) اگر امان دیدے آزاد مرد یا آزاد عورت کافرکو یا جماع کو یا اہل قلم کو یا اہل ہر کو اس کا امن دینا صحیح ہے اور کسی مسلمان کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے اس کا قتل کرنا مگر یہ کہ اس میں کوئی خرابی ہو۔ پس امام ان کے امن دینے کو تو ڑ دے۔ کسی کا فرکو یا کافر کی جماعت کو یا قلعے والے کو یا شہر والے کو آزاد مرد یا آزاد عورت امن دیدے تو سارے مسلمانوں کی جانب سے امن سمجھا جائے گا۔ اب کسی مسلمان کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اس کو قتل کرے۔ ہاں ! اگر اس کو امن دینے میں کوئی خرابی ہے تو امام با ضابطہ اس کے امن توڑنے کا اعلان کرے۔ پھر اس کے ساتھ جو معاملہ ہو کیا جائے۔ امان دینا ایک قسم کا عہد کرنا ہے کہ تم کو نہیں ماریں گے۔ اب اس کے خلاف کرنا قرآن میں مذموم ہے اس لئے یہ نہ کرے۔ آیت یہ ہے۔ الذين عاهدت منهم ثم ينقضون عهدهم في كل مرة وهم لا يتقون (ب) ( آیت ۵۶ ، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں عہد توڑنا کفار کی علامت بتائی گئی ہے اس لئے عہد توڑنا اچھا نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ۔ قال خطبنا على فقال ما عندنا كتاب نقرؤه الاكتاب الله وما في هذه الصحيفة ... وذمة المسلمين واحدة فمن اخفر مسلما فعليه مثل ذلك (ج) حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) غنیمت اس کو ملے گی جو جنگ میں شریک ہوا (الف) حضرت سلمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضرت طلحہ کا خادم تھا۔ ان کے گھوڑے کو پانی پلاتا ، اس کو ہنکا تا اور اس کی خدمت کرتا اور ان کے ساتھ ساتھ کھانا کھاتا پھر مجھ کو حضور نے دو حصے دیئے ، ایک حصہ گھوڑے کا ایک حصہ آدمی کا ( ب ) ان لوگوں میں سے جن سے آپ نے عہد کیا پھر وہ ہر مرتبہ عہد توڑتے ہیں پھر بچتے بھی نہیں (ج) حضرت علی نے ہم کو خطبہ دیا اور فرمایا میرے پاس کتاب اللہ کے علاوہ کوئی اور کتاب نہیں ہے جس کو ہم پڑھتے ہیں اور جو کچھ اس صحیفے میں ہے اور مسلمانوں کا ذمہ ایک ہے۔ جو کوئی مسلمانوں کے ذمے کو توڑے گا تو اس پر (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )  الشرح الثميرى الجزء الرابع ) ۲۶۷ كتاب السير فينبذ اليهم الامام ۳۰۱۵ (۳۶) ولا يجوز امان ذمى ولا اسير ولاتاجر يدخل عليهم ( بخاری شریف، باب ذمته السلمین وجوارهم واحدة یسعی با ادناهم بص۲۵۰، نمبر ۳۱۷۲) رمسلم شریف،باب فضل المدينه ودعا النبی و فیها بالبرکتة الخ ص ۴۴۰، نمبر ۱۳۷۰، کتاب الحج) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مسلمان کی ذمہ داری لینے سے تمام مسلمانوں کی ذمہ داری ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے کسی کو توڑنا نہیں چاہئے ۔ اور عورت کے امان کے سلسلے میں یہ حدیث ہے۔ انه سمع ام هاني ابنة ابي طالب تقول ... فقلت يا رسول الله ! زعم ابن امى على انه قاتل رجلا قد اجرته فلان بن هبيرة ، فقال رسول الله الا الله قد اجرنا من اجرت یا ام هانی. قالت امهانی ذلک ضحی (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب امان النساء وجوارحن، ص ۴۴۹، نمبر ۳۱۷ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب فی امان المرأة ، ج ۲، ص ۲۴، نمبر ۲۷۶۳) اس حدیث میں حضرت ام بھائی نے امن دیا تو حضور کی جانب سے امن مانا گیا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت امن دے تب بھی سب کی جانب سے امن ہو جائے گا۔ اگر امن برقرار رکھنے میں کوئی فساد ہو تو امام کو چاہئے کہ اعلان کر کے امن تو ڑے تا کہ وہ غفلت میں نہ رہے اور ہم عہد توڑنے کے مرتکب نہ ہوں۔ اس آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ واما تخافن من قوم خيانة فانبذ اليهم على سواء ان الله لا يحب الخائنين (ب) (سورة الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کسی قوم سے خیانت کا خطرہ ہو تو علی الاعلان اس کا عہد توڑ دو۔ اس لئے امام کو فساد کا خطرہ ہو تو علی الاعلان امان کو توڑ دے اور اس کی اطلاع دے۔ امن : باب تفعیل سے ہے، امن سے مشتق ہے امن دے، اہل حصن : قلعہ والے، بنبذ المهم : نبذ سے مشتق ہے پھینکنا، یہاں مراد ہے عہد توڑنا۔
Rules of aman. (3014) (35) If a free man or free woman gives aman to a kafir, or a group, or the people of a fortress, or a city, their giving aman is valid, and it is not permissible for any Muslim to kill them, unless there is some corruption in that. Then the imam should annul their aman. (Commentary:) When a free man or free woman gives aman to a kafir, a group of kafirs, the people of a fortress, or a city, it is considered aman from all Muslims. Now it is not permissible for any Muslim to kill him. However, if there is corruption in giving that aman, then the imam should officially announce its annulment, then deal with him accordingly. Granting aman is a kind of covenant that we will not kill you. Acting against it is condemned in the Qur'an, so one should not do it. The verse is: 'Those with whom you made a covenant, then they break their covenant every time, and they do not fear (Allah).' (Surah al-Anfal 8:56) In this verse, breaking a covenant is mentioned as a characteristic of the disbelievers, so breaking a covenant is not good. (2) There is a hadith: 'Ali addressed us and said: We have no book that we read except the Book of Allah and what is in this scroll... and the dhimma of the Muslims is one; whoever violates a Muslim's dhimma incurs the like thereof.' (Footnote: Previous page continuation) 'Spoils will be given to one who participated in war.' (a) Hadhrat Salama says: I was a servant of Hadhrat Talha... (b) 'Those with whom you made a covenant...' (c) Hadhrat Ali gave us a sermon... [PAGE_274] Al-Sharh al-Thamiri vol. 4, p. 267, Kitab al-Siyar. 'Then the imam should throw back to them (the treaty).' Section 3015 (36): And aman given by a dhimmi, a captive, or a trader who enters upon them is not valid. (Hadith citations). From this hadith, it is understood that the responsibility taken by one Muslim becomes the responsibility of all Muslims. Therefore, it should not be broken. And regarding a woman's aman, there is this hadith: He heard Umm Hani bint Abi Talib say... I said: O Messenger of Allah, my brother Ali claims that he will kill a man to whom I gave protection, so-and-so ibn Hubayra. The Messenger of Allah said: We have given protection to whom you gave protection, O Umm Hani. Umm Hani said that was at the time of Duha. (References). In this hadith, when Hadhrat Umm Hani gave aman, it was accepted from the Prophet's side. This shows that if a woman gives aman, it becomes aman from all. If there is corruption in maintaining the aman, the imam should announce and break the aman so that they do not remain unaware and we do not become guilty of breaking the covenant. There is proof of this in the verse: 'And if you fear treachery from a people, throw back to them (their treaty) on equal terms; indeed Allah does not love the treacherous.' (Surah al-Anfal 8:58) This verse says that if there is a risk of treachery from a people, then break the covenant openly. Therefore, if the imam fears corruption, he should break the aman openly and inform them. Aman: from the pattern taf'il, derived from amn, meaning 'he granted aman'. Ahl al-hisn: people of a fortress. Yambudh: derived from nabadh, meaning to throw, here meaning to break the covenant.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the grant of aman (safe conduct) by individual Muslims. The Hanafi position is that any free Muslim man or woman can grant aman to one or more kafir harbi, and it becomes binding on the entire Muslim community. No Muslim is permitted to kill the protected person as long as the aman remains in effect. However, if there is a clear maslaha (public interest) or mafsada (corruption), the imam has the authority to annul the aman publicly. The textual proofs are from the Qur'an (8:56, 8:58) which condemn breaking covenants and permit open annulment in case of treachery, and from the hadith of 'Ali about the unity of Muslim dhimma, and the hadith of Umm Hani which shows that even a woman's aman is valid and accepted by the Prophet himself. The commentary also includes a note that breaking aman without cause is akin to the characteristic of disbelievers. The lesson concludes with a glossary of terms related to aman.

Key Terms
امان (aman): Safe conduct or protection granted to a non-Muslim enemy (harbi), making it forbidden for Muslims to harm them.
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living permanently under Muslim rule with a pact of protection.
امام (imam): The ruler or leader of the Muslim community; has authority to annul aman for public interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should the imam do if there is corruption (mafsada) in maintaining the aman?
A) Silently revoke the aman.
B) Publicly announce the annulment of the aman.
C) Punish the person who gave the aman.
D) Consult the person who gave the aman.

Key Takeaway
Any free Muslim can grant aman that binds all Muslims; only the imam may annul it publicly for corruption.

Invalid Aman: Dhimmi, Prisoner, and Trader in Dar al-Harb
Ruling with proofs on invalid aman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on aman granted by a dhimmi, prisoner, or trader and explain the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Only free Muslims can grant effective aman; dhimmis, prisoners, and traders in dar al-harb cannot.

In the laws of jihad, the aman (safe conduct) given to an enemy combatant must be binding on the Muslim community. But not everyone can give aman. This lesson examines three categories whose aman is invalid according to the Hanafi school, backed by hadith and Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the main ruling: the aman of a dhimmi, a Muslim prisoner, and a Muslim trader in dar al-harb is invalid and not binding on the community.
2
Understand each category
Distinguish why each is invalid: dhimmi is non-Muslim, prisoner is under duress, trader may be coerced or fearful.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet said, 'The protection of Muslims is one; the lowest of them can be bound by it.' This shows only Muslims can grant binding aman.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Contrast with valid aman
The aman of a Muslim woman is valid, as proven by the hadith of Umm Hani where the Prophet confirmed her grant.
5
Note the Imam's authority to annul
If corruption is feared, the Imam may annul the aman publicly, based on Quran 8:58.

اس آیت میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ واما تخافن من قوم خيانة فانبذ اليهم على سواء ان الله لا يحب الخائنين (ب) (سورة الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں ہے کہ کسی قوم سے خیانت کا خطرہ ہو تو علی الاعلان اس کا عہد توڑ دو۔ اس لئے امام کو فساد کا خطرہ ہو تو علی الاعلان امان کو توڑ دے اور اس کی اطلاع دے۔ امن : باب تفعیل سے ہے، امن سے مشتق ہے امن دے، اہل حصن : قلعہ والے، بنبذ المهم : نبذ سے مشتق ہے پھینکنا، یہاں مراد ہے عہد توڑنا۔
[۳۰۱۵] (۳۶) زمی کا امان دینا جائز نہیں اور نہ قیدی کا اور نہ ایسے تاجروں کا جو ان کے یہاں جاتے ہوں۔

The Imam throws to them 3015 (36) And it is not permissible for a dhimmi, a prisoner, or a trader who enters upon them to grant aman. (Bukhari, chapter: The protection of Muslims is one, the lowest of them can be bound by it, p.250, no.3172) (Muslim, chapter: Virtue of Madinah and the Prophet's prayer for its blessing, p.440, no.1370, Book of Hajj) From this hadith it is known that taking the responsibility of one Muslim makes it the responsibility of all Muslims. Therefore, no one should break it. And regarding the aman of a woman, there is this hadith: that he heard Umm Hani bint Abi Talib saying... I said, O Messenger of Allah! My half-brother Ali claims he will kill a man whom I have given protection, so-and-so ibn Hubayrah. The Messenger of Allah said: Indeed, We have granted protection to whom you have granted protection, O Umm Hani. Umm Hani said that was at forenoon. (a) (Bukhari, chapter: The aman of women and their protection, p.449, no.317; Abu Dawud, chapter: Regarding the aman of a woman, vol.2, p.24, no.2763) From this hadith it is known that if a woman grants aman, then it becomes aman from everyone. If there is any corruption in maintaining the aman, the Imam should announce and break the aman so that they are not heedless and we do not commit breach of covenant.
There is proof in this verse: 'And if you fear treachery from a people, throw back to them on equal terms; indeed Allah does not love the treacherous.' (b) (Surah al-Anfal 8:58) In this verse it is that if there is fear of treachery from a people, then break the covenant openly. Therefore, if there is fear of corruption, the Imam should break the aman openly and inform them. 'Aman' is from the pattern taf'il, derived from amn, meaning to give aman. 'Ahl hisn': fort-dwellers. 'Binbuth': from nabhth, meaning to throw, here meaning to break the covenant.
[3015] (36) It is not permissible for a dhimmi to give aman, nor for a prisoner, nor for those traders who go to their land.
In our dar al-Islam, if a kafir is living as a dhimmi and gives aman to a harbi, his giving aman is not permissible. If one of our prisoners is in their custody and gives aman to a harbi, his aman is not considered. Or if a Muslim goes to dar al-harb for trade and, being influenced by the traders or fearing seizure of goods, gives aman to a harbi, his aman is not considered.
The dhimmi is not a Muslim. In the hadith, if any Muslim gives aman to a harbi, everyone must observe it. Therefore, the aman of a dhimmi is not considered. (2) The hadith clarifies: Ali ibn Abi Talib addressed us... The protection of Muslims is one; the lowest of them can be bound by it. And in another narration: Whoever breaks the covenant of a Muslim, upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people. No recompense or justice will be accepted from him on the Day of Resurrection.
Footnote: (from previous page) It is equal to sin. (a) Umm Hani said: I said, O Messenger of Allah! My half-brother Ali wants to kill a man whom I have given protection, so-and-so ibn Hubayrah. He said: Umm Hani, whom you have protected, I have also protected. Umm Hani said that this was at the time of forenoon. (b) Whom you fear treachery from, break the covenant with them openly. Allah does not love the treacherous.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that aman (safe conduct) granted by a dhimmi (protected non-Muslim), a Muslim prisoner, or a Muslim trader in dar al-harb is not valid. The author provides hadith evidence from Bukhari and Muslim that the protection of Muslims is one, implying only Muslims can grant it. The hadith of Umm Hani proves that a free Muslim woman can grant valid aman, as the Prophet confirmed it. The Quranic verse (8:58) supports the Imam's right to annul aman if there is fear of treachery. The commentary explains that dhimmis are not part of the Muslim covenant, prisoners are under duress, and traders may be coerced, so their aman is unreliable.

Key Terms
أمان (amān): Safe conduct or protection granted to a harbi, making his life and property inviolable during his stay in dar al-Islam.
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under the protection of the Islamic state, paying jizyah.
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim who is not under Muslim protection and with whom a state of war exists.
أسير (asīr): A Muslim prisoner captured by the enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling on Aman by a Slave: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on aman of a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a slave's aman, explain the Sahibayn's objection, and identify the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A slave's aman depends on permission to fight: Abu Hanifa requires it; Sahibayn accept it.

In the law of jihad, the grant of aman (safe conduct) to an enemy combatant is a serious act with binding consequences. This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether a slave can grant aman without his master's permission. As you read, note how each side argues from the nature of aman as an adjunct to fighting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the ikhtilaf
Find the act in question (aman by a slave) and the two positions: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn.
The matn opens with Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn's view follows.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's argument
He links aman to jihad: if a slave cannot fight without permission, he cannot grant aman without it.
This is a qiyas: aman is an 'arad (incidental) of jihad.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument
They cite the practice of Umar confirming the aman of a slave who actually fought.
Also the general principle that any Muslim's aman is binding.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's proof
The text notes that the incident involved a slave who participated in battle; it is specific, not general.
The response does not reject the incident but limits its scope.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, if a slave gives aman without permission, Abu Hanifa says it is invalid; Sahibayn say it is valid.
This affects the security of enemy combatants and the binding nature of aman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۱۶] (۳۷) ولا يجوز امان العبد عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى الا ان ياذن له مولاه. و صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا امن دینا صحیح ہے۔ آقا اگر غلام کو جنگ کرنے کی اجازت دی ہو پھر وہ غلام کسی حربی کو امن دے تو اس کا لحاظ کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر جنگ کی اجازت نہ دی ہو تو اس کے امان کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ جب وہ جنگ نہیں کر سکتا تو امان بھی نہیں دے سکتا۔ کیونکہ امن دینا جنگ کے عوارض میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے جب جنگ کا مجاز نہیں تو امان دینے کا مجاز نہیں ہونا چاہئے (۲) مصنف عبدالرزاق میں ایک لمبا واقعہ ہے جس میں یہ ہے کہ جنگ میں شریک ہونے والے غلام نے امان دیا تو حضرت عمرؓ نے لکھا کہ اس کا امن دینا جائز ہے۔ عن فضیل الرقاشي قال ... فقالوا امنتمونا واخرجوا الينا السهم، فيه کتاب امانهم فقلنا هذا عبـد والعبد لا يقدر على شيء قالوا لا ندرى عبدكم من حركم وقد خرجوا بامان قلنا فارجعوا بامان قالوا لا نرجع اليه ابدا فكتبنا الى عمر بعض قصتهم فكتب عمر ان العبد المسلم من المسلمين امانه امانهم (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الجوار و جوار العبد والمرأة، ج خامس ج ۲۳، نمبر ۹۴۳۶ سن لیبقی ، باب امان العبد، ج تاسع ، ص ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۰ ۱۸۱۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ العبد لا يقدر علی شیء جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ صحابہ جانتے تھے کہ غلام امان نہیں دے سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت علی نے فرمایا سب مسلمانوں کا ذمہ ایک ہے۔ آخری آدمی بھی اس کو پوری کرنے کی کوشش کرے گا۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ کوئی مسلمان عہد توڑے گا تو اس پر اللہ فرشتے اور تمام لوگوں کی لعنت ہے۔ اللہ قیامت کے دن نہ بدلہ قبول کرے گا اور نہ عدل ( ب ) ان کفار نے کہا تم لوگوں نے ہمیں امن دیا ہے۔ انہوں نے ہمارے سامنے تیر نکالا اس میں امان کا خط تھا۔ ہم نے کہا وہ غلام تھا اور غلام کسی چیز کی قدرت نہیں رکھتا۔ کفار نے کہا ہم تمہارے غلام اور آزاد کو نہیں جانتے۔ اور انہوں نے امان کا خط نکالا تو ہم نے کہا جاؤ امن کے ساتھ ۔ انہوں نے کہا ہم کبھی نہیں لوٹیں گے۔ ہم نے حضرت عمر کو بعض باتیں لکھیں تو حضرت عمر نے جواب دیا کہ غلام بھی مسلمان ہے اس کا امان بھی امان ہے۔
[3016] (37) According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), the aman of a slave is not valid unless his master permits him. The Sahibayn say that his aman is valid. If the master has given the slave permission to fight, then if that slave gives aman to a harbi, it will be considered. And if permission to fight was not given, then his aman is not considered. Since he cannot fight, he cannot give aman, because giving aman is one of the incidental matters of fighting. Therefore, when he is not authorized to fight, he should not be authorized to give aman. (2) In Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq there is a long incident in which a slave who participated in battle gave aman, and Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) wrote that his giving aman is valid. From Fudayl al-Raqqashi: ... They said: You gave us aman and they brought out to us an arrow in which there was a letter of aman. We said: This is a slave, and a slave has no power over anything. They said: We do not know your slave from your free man, and they came out with an aman. We said: Then return with aman. They said: We will never return to it. So we wrote to Umar about some of their story, and Umar wrote: The Muslim slave is from the Muslims; his aman is their aman. (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter: Protection and protection of slave and woman, vol.5, p.23, no.9436; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: Aman of slave, vol.9, p.120, no.1817) In this effect it is that the slave has no power over anything, meaning that the Companions knew that a slave cannot give aman.
Footnote: (a) Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The protection of all Muslims is one; the last of them will strive to fulfill it. In another narration: Whoever among Muslims breaks a covenant, upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people. Allah will not accept from him any substitute or justice on the Day of Resurrection. (b) The disbelievers said: You gave us aman, and they brought out an arrow in which there was a letter of aman. We said: He was a slave, and a slave has no power over anything. The disbelievers said: We do not know your slave from your free man, and they came out with an aman. We said: Go back with the aman. They said: We will never return. We wrote to Umar about some of their story, and Umar replied: The slave is a Muslim; his aman is also an aman.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of aman granted by a slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that a slave's aman is invalid unless the master has given him permission to fight, because aman is incidental to jihad. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that a slave's aman is valid based on the general principle that any Muslim's aman is binding, as seen in the incident from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq where Caliph Umar upheld the aman of a slave who had fought. The commentary also includes a footnote with the hadith about the unity of Muslims' protection and the curse on those who break a Muslim's covenant.

Key Terms
عبد (ʿabd): A male slave owned by a master.
مولى (mawlā): Master or owner of the slave.
أمان (amān): Safe conduct or protection granted to an enemy combatant.
حربي (ḥarbī): An enemy combatant not under Muslim protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of Abu Hanifa's ruling that a slave's aman is invalid without permission?
A) A hadith from Umar
B) The principle that aman is an ancillary matter of jihad
C) A verse from the Quran
D) Ijma of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The validity of a slave's aman in Hanafi fiqh depends on whether he has permission to fight; Abu Hanifa requires it, while the Sahibayn consider it valid based on the general principle and Umar's precedent.

8 min
The Validity of a Slave’s Aman in Jihad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on slave's aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on a slave's aman and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
A Muslim, even a slave, can grant aman — the highest authority is the Islamic identity, not the master's permission.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a slave can grant safe passage (aman) to an enemy without his master's permission to fight. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that aman is an accessory of fighting, so it is invalid unless the master permits fighting. The Sahibayn argue that any Muslim's aman is valid, citing explicit hadiths and the practice of 'Umar. The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn: the slave's aman is valid regardless of fighting permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn say regarding a slave's aman without fighting permission. Abu Hanifa says it is invalid; the Sahibayn say it is valid.
Abu Hanifa requires the master's permission to fight as a condition.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Understand why Abu Hanifa links aman to fighting permission: aman is an accessory of fighting, so one who cannot fight cannot grant aman. The athar of 'Umar initially shows Companions rejecting a slave's aman.
The athar is from Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq where Companions said 'a slave has no power over anything'.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
Review the hadith from 'Ali that the slave's aman is permissible, and the general principle that the covenant of Muslims is one and the lowest can grant aman.
The hadith explicitly says 'his aman is permissible when he gives aman to a people'.
4
Analyze the athar of 'Umar
Note that in the same incident, 'Umar ultimately ruled that the Muslim slave's aman is valid, showing the final practice supports the Sahibayn.
The athar ends with 'Umar writing that 'the Muslim slave is among the Muslims; his aman is their aman'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentary indicates that the stronger evidence supports the Sahibayn, making their view the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The hadith from 'Ali is explicit and the general principle is sound.

And the aman of a slave is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, unless his master permits him to fight. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: His aman is valid. (A) (Muslim Sharif, Bab Fadl al-Madina... Bukhari Sharif, Bab Dhimmat al-Muslimin...) This hadith contains 'dhimmat al-muslimin' from which it is understood that the aman of a Muslim is worthy of consideration, not that of a dhimmi. (2) A dhimmi would anyway protect a harbi without cause; if we consider his aman, we would not be able to fight the harbi. Therefore the aman of a dhimmi is not considered. The aman of a captive is not considered because he is under their control. The second point is that he would grant aman to every harbi, then how would war be waged? Therefore the aman of a captive is not considered. Similarly, our merchants who go to dar al-harb either influenced by them or fearing seizure of goods will grant aman, not with freedom of heart and pleasure. Therefore their aman is also not considered. Khut asir: captive. [3016] (37) According to Imam Abu Hanifa, a slave granting aman is not permissible unless his master permits fighting. And the Sahibayn say that his granting aman is valid. If the master permitted the slave to fight, then if that slave grants aman to a harbi, it will be considered. And if he did not permit fighting, then his aman is not considered. When he cannot fight, he cannot grant aman either. Because granting aman is among the accessories of fighting. Therefore, when he is not authorized to fight, he should not be authorized to grant aman. (2) In Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq there is a long incident in which a slave who participated in fighting granted aman, and 'Umar (RA) wrote that his granting aman is permissible. From Fudayl al-Riqashi... they said: You gave us aman, and they brought out the arrow containing the letter of aman. We said: This is a slave, and a slave has no power over anything. They said: We do not know your slave from your free, and they came out with aman. We said: Return with aman. They said: We will never return to it. We wrote to 'Umar about their story, and 'Umar wrote: The Muslim slave is among the Muslims; his aman is their aman. (B) (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq... Sunan al-Bayhaqi... ) In this athar it is that 'a slave has no power over anything', meaning the Companions knew that a slave cannot grant aman. Footnote: (A) 'Ali said: The covenant of all Muslims is one; even the lowest of them will strive to fulfill it. Another narration: Whoever Muslim breaks a covenant, upon him is the curse of Allah, the angels, and all people. Allah will accept neither recompense nor justice on the Day of Judgment. (B) Those disbelievers said: You have given us aman. They brought out the arrow, and in it was the letter of aman. We said: He was a slave, and a slave has no power. The disbelievers said: We do not know your slave from your free, and they brought out the letter of aman. So we said: Go with aman. They said: We will never return. We wrote some of the matter to 'Umar, and 'Umar replied: The slave is a Muslim; his aman is aman. And the second point is that this slave was participating in fighting, so his aman was accepted. Therefore, if he participates in fighting, his aman will be accepted; otherwise not. The Sahibayn say: whether he participates in fighting or not, his aman is valid. He is also a Muslim, and the aman of a Muslim is valid. Therefore the aman of a slave will be valid; the hadith has passed, 'dhimmat al-muslimin wahidah yas'a biha adnahum' (Muslim Sharif...). (2) The hadith specifies it: from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib that the Messenger of Allah said: Indeed, there is nothing for the slave from the spoils except some insignificant belongings, and his aman is permissible when he gives aman to a people. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi... Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) This hadith explicitly states that even if the slave does not participate in fighting, his aman is valid. Therefore the slave's aman is valid. (3) In the athar of 'Umar above, it was also that the slave's aman is valid.
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a slave granting aman (safe passage) to an enemy combatant. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs. The author begins by stating the ruling: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, a slave's aman is not valid unless his master has permitted him to fight. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the slave's aman is valid regardless. The commentary then elaborates on the reasoning. For Abu Hanifa, granting aman is an accessory of fighting (min 'awarid al-qital). Since a slave without permission lacks authority to fight, he also lacks authority to grant aman. The commentary supports this with an athar from 'Umar where the Companions initially rejected a slave's aman because 'a slave has no power over anything'. However, in that same incident, 'Umar ultimately accepted the aman because the slave was a Muslim. The Sahibayn argue based on the general principle that the aman of any Muslim is valid, citing the hadith 'the covenant of Muslims is one, and the lowest of them can grant it' and a specific hadith from 'Ali that a slave's aman is permissible even if he does not fight. The commentary discusses both views and the supporting evidence, showing that the Hanafi school has two positions, with the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) being that of the Sahibayn, as indicated by the later hadith and 'Umar's ruling. The passage also distinguishes the slave's case from that of a dhimmi, captive, or merchant, whose aman is invalid for various reasons.

Key Terms
امان (aman): Safe passage or guarantee of security granted to an enemy combatant, making their person and property inviolable for the duration.
عبد (abd): Slave, specifically a male slave who may or may not be permitted to fight in jihad.
ذمة (dhimma): Covenant or guarantee of protection and rights, especially for non-Muslim subjects or fellow Muslims.
صاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two Companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is required for a slave's aman to be valid?
A) The slave must have permission from his master to fight.
B) The slave must be participating in the battle.
C) The slave's aman is valid regardless of permission to fight.
D) The slave must be a free Muslim.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that a Muslim slave's aman is valid, supported by the hadith that the covenant of Muslims is one and the lowest can grant it.

Ownership by Conquest in Jihad: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on ownership through conquest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership transfer via ghalaba between kuffar and when Muslims conquer them, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on ghalaba.

Core Idea
Domination in war transfers ownership; Muslim conquest supersedes all prior ownership.

This lesson addresses a key fiqh issue in jihad: what happens to property when one group of disbelievers conquers another, and then Muslims conquer them. The Hanafi position is that ghalaba (overcoming) with transfer to one's own territory causes ownership to pass, and Muslim conquest makes all such property lawful spoils (ghanimah). Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal status of war booty in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn presents two cases: (1) Turks overcoming Romans, and (2) Muslims overcoming Turks. Isolate each scenario and its stated ruling.
The commentary explains the reasoning for each.
2
Extract the ruling per scenario
For scenario (1): the Turks own the captives and property of the Romans. For scenario (2): whatever Muslims find among the Turks (including prior Roman property) is halal (lawful) for them as spoils.
Note that the ruling for scenario (2) does not distinguish between property originally Turkish or Roman.
3
Identify the cause (illah) of ownership transfer
The commentary states the reason for ownership is ghalaba (domination) and transfer into one's own territory (al-ghalabah wa idkhal fi mamlakatih). This applies to both kuffar and Muslims, but with the additional principle of ghanimah for Muslims.
For kuffar, ownership through capture is recognized, but for Muslims, it is additionally sanctified as ghanimah.
4
Apply the analogy to Muslim conquest
Since kuffar become owners of property they capture from other kuffar, when Muslims conquer those kuffar, Muslims inherit ownership of all property in their possession, regardless of its origin.
This is supported by Quranic reference (though not fully quoted here).
5
Conclude the practical ruling
After Muslim conquest, all property found among the defeated kuffar becomes ghanimah, owned by the Muslim combatants after the imam's distribution.
This includes both property originally belonging to the defeated kuffar and property they had seized from others.

[3017] (38) And if the Turks overcome the Romans, take them captive, and take their property, they own it. [3018] (39) And if we overcome them, then what we find among them is halal for us. 'Turks' and 'Romans' refer to disbelievers. That is, when the people of one disbelieving country overcome the people of another disbelieving country, capture their people, and take possession of their property, they become owners of it. When a disbeliever takes possession of a Muslim's property, they become owners; so when they take possession of a disbeliever's property, why would they not become owners? (2) The reason for ownership is domination and taking into their own territory, and this is found, so they become owners. Sabw: derived from 'saba', meaning captivity. Turk: a country that was formerly a disbelieving country. Rum: a country near Turk that is still a disbelieving country. [3018] (39) And if we overcome the Turks, then what we find among them is halal for us. If we attack and overcome the Turks, then the property that the Turks took from the Romans all comes into the hands of Muslims, so we also become owners of it. And whatever original property of the Turks comes into our hands, we also become owners of it. After domination in jihad, all that property is spoils, and spoils are owned by Muslims. Therefore, whether it is the Turks' own property or property taken from the Romans, i.e., whether it is the property of a harbi or property taken from another harbi, the Muslim becomes owner of both. Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings related to ownership through conquest (ghalaba). The passage type is a ruling statement with rational explanation. First, the matn states: if the Turks (a kafir nation) overpower the Romans (another kafir nation), take them captive and seize their property, the Turks become owners of that property. The commentary explains that this is because domination (ghalaba) and transfer to their own territory establishes ownership. It draws an analogy: if a kafir becomes owner of a Muslim's property through capture, similarly when kafirs capture from other kafirs, ownership transfers. Second, if Muslims overcome the Turks, whatever we find among them (including property originally taken from Romans) is halal for us as spoils of war (ghanimah). The commentary clarifies that after Muslim conquest, all property in the hands of the defeated kafirs becomes spoils, whether it was originally their own or acquired from other kafirs. The reasoning is that in jihad, spoils belong to Muslims. The passage ends with a reference to a Quranic verse (not quoted), implying scriptural support. The overall principle is that ownership transfers through conquest between belligerent parties, and Muslims inherit that ownership when they conquer.

Key Terms
غلب (ghalaba): Overcoming/domination in warfare, leading to ownership of captives and property.
غنيمة (ghanimah): Spoils of war taken from the enemy after military victory, which become property of the Muslim combatants after the imam's distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for Muslims when they overcome a kafir group that had previously taken property from another kafir group?
A) The property must be returned to the original kafir owners.
B) The property becomes halal for Muslims as spoils of war.
C) The property remains the property of the defeated kafir group.
D) The property is considered ownerless and can be taken by anyone.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ownership transfers through conquest (ghalaba), and when Muslims conquer, all property found with the enemy becomes lawful spoils of war (ghanimah).

Ownership of Spoils among Non-Muslims: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on kuffar owning spoils taken from other kuffar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ownership of property seized by one non-Muslim group from another and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) by analogy.

Core Idea
When disbelievers overpower other disbelievers and bring the spoils into their own land, they become owners by analogy with Muslims.

This passage clarifies a specific ruling in the law of war (siyar): the status of property taken by one group of non-Muslims from another. Using a simple analogy, the Hanafi school affirms that the victors gain ownership if they satisfy two conditions: overpowering (ghalaba) and transfer to their own territory (ihraz). We will examine the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: Turks overpower Romans, take captives and property. The ruling: they become the owners.
2
Locate the analogy (qiyas)
The author compares to the case where disbelievers capture Muslim property: they become owners. By analogy, they become owners of other disbelievers' property.
The original case (asl) is kuffar capturing Muslim property.
3
Identify the effective cause (illa)
The illa is overpowering (ghalaba) and taking into one's own land (ihraz). Both are present in this scenario.
4
Note the conditions for ownership
Ownership is conditional on both ghalaba and ihraz. If either is missing, ownership is not established.
For example, if they seize property but do not bring it to their land, they do not become owners.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۱۷] (۳۸) واذا غلب الترك على الروم فسَبوهم واخذوا اموالهم ملكوها جب مسلمان کے مال پر کافرقبضہ کر لیتے ہیں تو وہ مالک ہو جاتے ہیں تو کافر کے ملک پر قبضہ کریں گے تو کیوں مالک نہیں ہوں گے؟ (۲) مالک ہونے کی وجہ غلبہ ہونا اور اپنے ملک کے اندر لے جانا ہے اور یہ پایا گیا اس لئے وہ مالک ہو جائیں گے۔ سبو : سی سے مشتق ہے قید کرنا، ترک : ایک ملک ہے جو پہلے کافر ملک تھا، روم : ترک کے پاس ایک ملک ہے جو ابھی تک کافر ملک ہی ہے۔
(38) And if the Turks overpower the Romans, take them captive, and seize their property, they become its owners. When Muslims' property is seized by disbelievers, they become owners; so if they seize property of another disbeliever, why would they not become owners? The reason for ownership is overpowering and taking it into their own land, and this is found here, so they become owners. 'Sabo' is derived from 'saby' meaning to take captive. 'Turk' is a country that was previously a disbeliever country. 'Rum' is a country near Turk that is still a disbeliever country.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage states a clear ruling: when one group of disbelievers (here the Turks) overpowers another group (the Romans), capturing them and seizing their property, the victorious group becomes the legal owners of that property. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on a parallel: if disbelievers capture Muslim property, they become owners (by the principle of conquest and transfer to dar al-harb). Similarly, when they capture property from other disbelievers, the same principle applies, so they also become owners. The key factors are (1) overpowering (ghalaba) and (2) transporting the property into their own territory (ihraz). Both conditions are satisfied here. The commentary also provides lexical clarifications: 'sabo' means taking captives; 'Turk' refers to a land that was originally kafir; 'Rum' refers to a neighboring land that remains kafir. This ruling is not about Muslims but about the relationship between two non-Muslim parties.

Key Terms
غلب (ghalaba): To overpower or conquer, leading to ownership of spoils.
ملكوها (malakūhā): They become its owners (literally 'they own it').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If they only capture the Romans without taking property.
B) If they overpower them and take the property into their own land.
C) If the Romans are Muslims.
D) If the property is movable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, non-Muslim belligerents can own spoils taken from other non-Muslim belligerents if they overpower and take the spoils into their own territory.

Spoils Include Property Captured from a Previous Enemy
Ruling on spoils when Muslims conquer Turks who previously conquered Romans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that all property of a harbi, including property he previously captured from another harbi, becomes spoils upon Muslim conquest, and identify the primary textual evidence.

Core Idea
A harbi's entire captured property — even that taken from another enemy — becomes spoils.

This passage extends the general principle of ghanimah to a specific scenario: when Muslims conquer an enemy (the Turks) who had previously plundered another enemy (the Romans). Are those Roman assets now spoils for Muslims? The Hanafi school answers with a clear yes, backed by Quranic verses and prophetic practice. Understanding this ruling clarifies the scope of ownership in jihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage describes a situation where Muslims overpower the Turks, and among the captured property are items that the Turks had earlier taken from the Romans. Identify the two categories of property involved: the Turks' original property and their loot from the Romans.
Both categories are considered harbi property.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that all of this property becomes lawful spoils (ghanimah) for the Muslims, regardless of its original ownership. Confirm that the hukm is halal and owned by the Muslims.
No distinction is made between property originally belonging to the Turks and that seized from Romans.
3
Analyze the Quranic Evidence
Examine the two Quranic verses cited: Surah al-Hashr 59:7 (on fay) and Surah al-Anfal 8:69 (on ghanimah). Understand how 'fay' is interpreted broadly to include spoils, and how 'kulu' (eat) indicates permission and ownership.
The imperative implies unrestricted ownership of what is captured.
4
Analyze the Sunnah Evidence
Consider the example of the Prophet distributing the land of Khaybar, which was conquered from Jews who themselves had acquired it from others. This shows that the original source does not affect the spoils status.
Khaybar land was ghanimah, even though it had been owned by different groups over time.
5
Reflect on the Implication
Understand the practical result: if property is found with a harbi enemy at the time of capture, its previous history (even if stolen from another non-Muslim) does not prevent it from being spoils for Muslims.
This prevents complex disputes about chain of ownership.

(39) And if we overpower the Turks, it is lawful for us whatever we find of that. When we attacked and overpowered the Turks, the property that the Turks had taken from the Romans came into the hands of the Muslims, so we become owners of that as well. And also the original property of the Turks that comes into our hands, we become owners of that too. After overpowering in jihad, all that property is spoils, and spoils are owned by the Muslims. Therefore, in jihad, whether it is property belonging to the Turks themselves or property seized from the Romans, i.e., the property of a harbi or property seized from another harbi, in both cases the Muslims become owners. Evidence from the Quran: 'What Allah has bestowed on His Messenger from the people of the townships belongs to Allah, to the Messenger, and to the near of kin, orphans, the needy, and the wayfarer, so that it does not become a commodity circulating among the wealthy among you.' (Surah al-Hashr 59:7) This verse indicates that the fay (spoils) given by Allah is owned by you. Another verse: 'So eat from what you have taken as spoils, lawful and good, and fear Allah; indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' (Surah al-Anfal 8:69) This verse indicates that the spoils you obtain are halal for you, proving that Muslims become owners upon capturing harbi property. Also, the Prophet (peace be upon him) distributed the land of Khaybar among the mujahideen. (Abu Dawud, chapter on the ruling of Khaybar land, vol. 2 p. 68 no. 3010).
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous ruling: when Muslims overpower the Turks (who are harbi kuffar), the spoils they obtain include both the original property of the Turks and the property the Turks had previously taken from the Romans. All of this becomes ghanimah (spoils) and is owned by the Muslims. The ruling is supported by multiple proofs. First, a general principle: any property of a harbi that Muslims capture becomes ghanimah. Second, two Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Hashr 59:7 speaks of fay (which in this context includes spoils) as belonging to the community; Surah al-Anfal 8:69 explicitly permits consuming spoils as halal, implying ownership. Third, the practical example of the Prophet distributing the land of Khaybar to the Companions after conquest. These evidences establish that Muslims acquire full ownership of harbi property upon conquest, regardless of whether that property originally belonged to the conquered enemy or was taken from another enemy.

Key Terms
غنيمة (ghanīmah): Spoils taken from the enemy during jihad, which become property of the Muslim community.
حربي (ḥarbī): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, whose property is permissible to take as spoils.

All property captured from a harbi, including property he previously took from another enemy, becomes ghanimah for Muslims upon conquest.

Enemy Captures Muslim Property: Ownership and Dispute with Shafi'i
Ruling on kuffar owning Muslim property they capture and the Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ownership of captured Muslim property by disbelievers and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using textual evidence.

Core Idea
When disbelievers capture Muslim property and take it to dar al-harb, they become its owners — but only if they complete iḥrāz.

This passage presents a significant legal dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the ownership of Muslim property captured by enemy forces. The Hanafi school holds that once the property is taken into dar al-harb (the abode of war), the disbelievers become its owners, based on Quranic and prophetic evidence. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing a hadith to argue that ownership does not transfer. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi approach to property rights in warfare and the use of textual sources.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: disbelievers become owners of captured Muslim property when they perform iḥrāz (taking it to dar al-harb).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite view: ownership does not transfer to the disbelievers.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Ibn 'Umar's slave, which the Shafi'i school uses as evidence against ownership transfer.
The slave fled to the enemy, was later recovered, and the Prophet returned him to Ibn 'Umar.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi distinction: the case of a fleeing slave is different from property captured in war; hence the hadith does not contradict the general principle.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical outcome: if ownership transfers, recovered property is spoils; if not, it reverts to the original owner.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۰۱۹] (۴۰) واذا غلبوا على اموالنا واحرزوها ہمارے مال پر غالب آجائیں اور دار الحرب میں لے جائیں اور اس کو دار الحرب لے کر چلے جائیں تو وہ اس کے مال ہو جائیں گے۔ پہلے بتایا کہ غلبہ کر کے اپنے ملک میں لے جانے سے مالک بن جاتے ہیں اس لئے حربی مالک ہو جائیں گے (۲) آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ للفقراء المهاجرين الذين أخرجوا من ديارهم وأموالهم يبتغون فضلا من الله ورضوانا (ج) (آیت ۸، سورة الحشر ۵۹) اس آیت میں مکہ مکرمہ کے مہاجرین کو فقراء کہا گیا۔ حالانکہ ان کے پاس مال تھا پھر بھی فقراء کہنا اس بات پر دلالت ہے کہ اس کے مال پر کفار کا قبضہ ہو گیا اور وہ اس کا مالک بن گئے۔ اسی لئے تو مہاجرین کو فقراء کہا گیا ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن أسامة بن زيد أنه قال يا رسول الله! أين تنزل في دارك بمكة؟ فقال وهل ترك عقيل من رباع ودور (د) (بخاری شریف، باب توریث دور مکة و شرائها الخ ص ٢١٦، نمبر ١٥٨٨، کتاب الحج؛ مسلم شریف، باب نزول الحاج بمكة و توریث دورها ص ٢٣٦، نمبر ١٣٥) اس حدیث میں حضور نے سوال کے طور پر پوچھا کیا عقیل نے کوئی گھر بازمین کا ٹکڑا ہمارے لئے چھوڑا ہے جہاں میں ٹھہروں؟ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کی زمین اور مکان پر حضرت عقیل جو اس وقت کافر تھے قبضے کے بعد وہ مالک ہو گئے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفار ہمارے مال پر قبضہ کرلے تو وہ مالک ہو جائیں گے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کفار ہمارے مالوں کے مالک نہیں بنیں گے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابن عمر کا غلام دشمن کی طرف بھاگا اور اس نے اس پر قبضہ بھی کر لیا پھر اس پر غلبہ پایا تو اس غلام کو حضور نے حضرت ابن عمر کی طرف واپس کر دیا۔ اور اس کو مسلمانوں میں تقسیم نہیں فرمایا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب کے زمانے میں بھی غلام حضرت ابن عمر ہی کا رہا، دشمن مالک نہیں بنا۔
(40) And if they overpower us regarding our property and take it into their land (ihraz), they become its owners. Earlier it was stated that by overpowering and taking to their own land, they become owners, so the harbi will become owner. (2) There is an indication of this in the Quran: 'For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure.' (Surah al-Hashr 59:8) In this verse, the emigrants from Mecca are called poor (fuqara), despite having property. This indicates that the disbelievers had seized their property and became owners of it. That is why the emigrants were called poor. (2) Also, there is proof from hadith: From Usama ibn Zayd that he said: O Messenger of Allah, where will you alight in your house in Mecca? He replied: Did 'Aqil leave any dwelling or property? (Bukhari, chapter on inheritance of houses in Mecca, p.216 no.1588, book of Hajj; Muslim, chapter on descent of pilgrim in Mecca and inheritance of its houses, p.236 no.135). In this hadith, the Prophet asked rhetorically whether 'Aqil (who was then a disbeliever) had left any property for him to stay in. This shows that after 'Aqil's possession, he became owner of the Prophet's land and house. Thus, when disbelievers capture our property, they become owners. Imam al-Shafi'i says that disbelievers will not become owners of our property. He argues that a slave of Ibn 'Umar fled to the enemy and they took possession, but later when the Muslims overcame, the Prophet returned the slave to Ibn 'Umar and did not distribute him among the Muslims as spoils. This proves that even in dar al-harb, the slave remained Ibn 'Umar's property; the enemy did not become owner.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when disbelievers capture Muslim property and take it into dar al-harb (the abode of war). The Hanafi position is that they become owners, based on the principle that capturing and taking to their territory transfers ownership. Evidence from the Quran: Allah calls the Muhajirun 'poor' because the kuffar had seized their property, implying the kuffar owned it. Evidence from hadith: The Prophet's asking about 'Aqil's possession of his (the Prophet's) property in Mecca indicates that 'Aqil (then a kafir) became owner by capture. Then the passage presents the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that kuffar do not become owners. He cites the incident of Ibn 'Umar's slave who fled to the enemy; when the Muslims recovered him, the Prophet returned him to Ibn 'Umar, not distributing him as spoils. The Hanafi response (implicit) is that the case of a slave who fled is different: he is not captured in war but defected, so ownership does not transfer. The discussion highlights a practical difference: if kuffar become owners, their subsequent sale or disposition is valid; if not, then when Muslims recover the property, it reverts to the original Muslim owner without the need for spoils distribution.

Key Terms
احراز (iḥrāz): Taking captured property into the enemy's own territory (dar al-harb), a condition for ownership transfer.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): The land of war, i.e., territory under the control of non-Muslims who are at war with Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Quranic verse calling Muhajirun poor.
B) The hadith of 'Aqil's possession.
C) The incident of Ibn 'Umar's slave returned by the Prophet.
D) The principle that Muslims never lose ownership.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that disbelievers become owners of Muslim property once they capture it and take it into their territory (iḥrāz), and this is supported by Quran and hadith, with the Shafi'i objection being distinguished as a different case.
