Enemy Ownership of Captured Muslim Property: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on enemy ownership of captured property with dalil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on enemy ownership of captured Muslim property, identify the key proofs, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
When the enemy ihraz (takes) Muslim property into dar al-harb, Hanafi says they own it; Shafi'i disagrees.

In this passage, the author establishes the Hanafi ruling that the enemy (harbi) becomes the owner of Muslim property they capture and transport to dar al-harb. He then presents the Shafi'i objection and responds with a distinction between recovery before and after booty division. This lesson walks through the proofs and the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

كتاب السير

الترك حل لنا ما نجده من ذلک ۱۳۰۱۹ (۴۰) واذا غلبوا على اموالنا واحرزوها اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ ما افـاء الـلـه على رسوله من اهل القرى فلله وللرسول ولذى القربى واليتمى والمساكين وابن السبيل كي لا يكون دوله بين الاغنياء منكم (الف) ( آیت ۷، سورۃ الحشر ۵۹) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اللہ نے جو فی یعنی مال غنیمت دیا وہ تم لوگوں کی ملکیت ہے (۳) دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ فكـلـوا مـمـا غـنـمـتـم حلالا طيبا واتقوا الله ان الله غفور رحيم (ب) ( آیت ۶۹ ، سورۃ الانفال (۸) اس آیت میں ہے جو مال غنیمت تم کو ملا اس کو كھاؤ وہ تمہارے لئے حلال ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی کے مال پر قبضہ کرنے سے مسلمان مالک ہو جائیں گے (۳) حضور نے خیبر کی زمین کو مجاہدین میں تقسیم فرمائی (ابو داؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فی حکم ارض خیبر ، ج ۲، ص ۶۸ نمبر ۳۰۱۰) [ ۳۰۱۹] (۴۰) اور اگر وہ ہمارے مال پر غالب آجائیں اور دار الحرب میں لے جائیں اور اس کو دار الحرب لے کر چلے جائیں تو وہ اس کے مال ہو جائیں گے۔

پہلے بتایا کہ غلبہ کر کے اپنے ملک میں لے جانے سے مالک بن جاتے ہیں اس لئے حربی مالک ہو جائیں گے (۲) آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ للفقراء المهاجرين الذين اخرجوا من ديارهم واموالهم يبتغون فضلا من الله ورضوانا (ج) (آیت ۸ ،سورة الحشر ۵۹) اس آیت میں مکہ مکرمہ کے مہاجرین کو فقراء کہا گیا۔ حالانکہ ان کے پاس مال تھا پھر بھی فقراء کہنا اس بات پر دلالت ہے کہ اس کے مال پر کفار کا قبضہ ہو گیا اور وہ اس کا مالک بن گئے۔ اسی لئے تو مہاجرین کو فقراء کہا گیا ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن اسامة بن زيد انه قال يا رسول الله ! این تنزل في دارك بمكة ؟ فقال وهل ترك عقيل من رباع و دور (د) ( بخاری شریف، باب تو ریٹ دور مکتہ و معها وشرائها الخ ص ۲۱۶، نمبر ۱۵۸۸، کتاب الحج رمسلم شریف، باب نزول الحاج بمکته و توریث دورها ص ۲۳۶، نمبر (۱۳۵) اس حدیث میں حضور نے سوال کے طور پر پوچھا کیا عقیل نے کوئی گھر باز مین کا ٹکڑا ہمارے لئے چھوڑا ہے جہاں میں ٹھہروں؟ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کی زمین اور مکان پر حضرت عقیل جو اس وقت کا فر تھے قبضے کے بعد وہ مالک ہو گئے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفار ہمارے مال پر قبضہ کرلے تو وہ مالک ہو جائیں گے۔

امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ کفار ہمارے مالوں کے مالک نہیں بنیں گے۔

وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابن عمر کا غلام دشمن کی طرف بھاگا اور اس نے اس پر قبضہ بھی کر لیا پھر اس پر غلبہ پایا تو اس غلام کو حضور نے حضرت ابن عمر کی طرف واپس کر دیا۔ اور اس کو مسلمانوں میں تقسیم نہیں فرمایا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ دارالحرب کے زمانے میں بھی غلام حضرت ابن عمر کی ملکیت رہی، حربی اس کا مالک نہ بن سکا۔ ان غلاما لابن عمر آبق الى العدو فظهر عليه المسلمون فرده رسول الله له الى ابن عمر ولم يقسم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی المال صیہ العدو من السلمين ثم یدر که صاحبه في الغنيمة ج ۲ ص ۱۸، نمبر ۲۶۲۹۸ ر بخاری شریف ، باب اذ اغنم المشرکون مال المسلم ثم وجده المسلم می ۲۳۱، نمبر ۳۰۶۸) اس حدیث میں غلام حضرت ابن عمر گو واپس کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی اس کا مالک نہیں بن سکا۔ احرز : جمع کرنا ، ایک ملک سے دوسرے ملک میں مال لے جانا۔

لنت

(۳۰۲۰ (۳۱) اگر اس پر مسلمان غالب آجا ئیں اور اس کو تقسیم سے پہلے پائیں تو وہ ان کےلئے ہوگا بغیر کسی عوض کے، اور اگر اس کو تقسیم کے بعد پایا تو اس کو قیمت سے لے اگر چاہیں۔

حربیوں نے ہمارے مال پر قبضہ کیا تھا اب مسلمانوں نے اس پر دھاوا بول کر مال واپس لے لیا تو اگر تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے مالک نے اس مال کو پالیا تو اس کو مالک لے لے گا اور اس کے بدلے میں کچھ نہیں دے گا۔ اور اگر تقسیم ہو چکا تو جس کے ہاتھ میں گیا اس کو قیمت دے کر اپنی چیز لے۔ اور اگر قیمت دے کر نہ لینا چاہے تو نہ لے۔

تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے مال غنیمت کا مال ہے کسی مجاہد کی ملکیت نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے اس کو بغیر کسی قیمت سے لے لینے میں حرج نہیں ہے (۲) چونکہ پہلے اس کی چیز تھی اس لئے اس کو ہی دے دی جائے گی (۳) اوپر کی حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت تھا۔ عن ابن عمر ان غلاما لابن عـمـر ابـق الى العدو فظهر عليه المسلمون فرده رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الى ابن عمر ولم يقسم (ب) ابوداؤد شریف، باب المال يصيبه العدو من المسلمين ، ج ۲، ص ۱۲، نمبر ۲۶۹۸ / بخاری شریف، از اغنم المشرکون مال المسلم ثم وجده المسلم ص ۲۳۱، نمبر ۳۰۶۷) اس حدیث میں تقسیم سے پہلے مالک نے مال پایا تو اس کو مالک کی طرف واپس کر دیا گیا۔

اور تقسیم ہو گیا ہو تو قیمت دے کر مالک سے لے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فيما احرز العدو فاستنقذه المسلمون منهم او اخذه صاحبه قبل ان يقسم فهو احق فان وجده وقد قسم ، فان شاء اخذه بالثمن (ج) (دار قطنی ، کتاب السیر ، ج رابع ، ص ۶۴ نمبر ۴۱۵۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تقسیم ہو چکی ہو تو قیمت سے واپس لے۔

حاشیہ : (الف) اللہ نے اپنے رسول کو اہل قری کے مالوں میں سے زیادہ اللہ کے لئے رسول، رشتہ دار اور یتیم اور مسکین اور مسافر کے لئے ہے تاکہ تمہارے مالداروں کے درمیان دولت نہ بن جائے (ب) جو کچھ مال غنیمت آیا اس کو کھاؤ حلال طبیب ہے اور اللہ سے تقوی اختیار کرو اللہ معاف کرنے والے ہیں (ج) فقراء مہاجرین کے لئے جو اپنے گھروں اور مالوں سے نکالے گئے ہیں اللہ کا فضل اور رضامندی تلاش کرتے ہیں۔ (و) حضرت اسامہ بن زید نے پو چھایا رسول اللہ! آپ مکہ کے گھروں میں کہاں اتریں گے؟ جواب دیا کیا عقیل نے کوئی زمین یا گھر چھوڑا ہے؟

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عمر کا ایک غلام دشمن کی طرف بھاگ گیا۔ پھر مسلمان اس پر قابض ہوئے تو حضور نے ابن عمر کی طرف لوٹا دیا اور تقسیم نہیں کی (ب) حضرت ابن عمر کا ایک غلام دشمن کی طرف بھاگ گیا۔ پھر مسلمان اس پر قابض ہوئے تو حضور نے اس کو ابن عمر کی طرف لوٹا دیا اور تقسیم نہیں کی (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کا فردشمن جو کچھ ہم سے لے لے پھر مسلمان اس سے واپس لوٹالے یا چیز کا مالک تقسیم ہونے سے پہلے اس کو لے لے تو وہ زیادہ حقدار ہے۔ اور اگر تقسیم ہونے کے بعد پائے تو چاہے تو قیمت سے لے۔
Book of Siyar

The solution for us regarding what we find of that is: 13019 (40) And if they overcome our property and take it away, its proof is: 'Whatever Allah has restored to His Messenger from the people of the towns, it is for Allah and the Messenger and for the near of kin and orphans and the needy and the wayfarer, so that it does not become a thing circulated among the wealthy among you' (Surah al-Hashr 59:7). In this verse, whatever booty Allah has given is the ownership of you people. Another verse: 'So eat of what you have captured as booty, lawful and good, and fear Allah; indeed Allah is Forgiving and Merciful' (Surah al-Anfal 8:69). In this verse, whatever booty you have obtained, eat it; it is lawful for you. From this it is understood that the Muslims become owners upon taking possession of the harbi's property. The Prophet (peace be upon him) divided the land of Khaybar among the mujahideen (Abu Dawud). [3019] (40) And if they overcome our property and take it to dar al-harb and take it to dar al-harb, they become its owners.

Earlier it was stated that by overcoming and taking to their own country, they become owners; therefore the harbi will become owners. The verse indicates: 'For the poor emigrants who were expelled from their homes and their properties, seeking bounty from Allah and approval' (Surah al-Hashr 59:8). In this verse, the emigrants of Mecca are called poor, although they had property. Nevertheless, calling them poor indicates that the disbelievers had taken possession of their property and became owners. That is why the emigrants are called poor. There is proof from hadith: From Usama ibn Zayd that he said: 'O Messenger of Allah, where will you alight in your house in Mecca?' He said: 'Did Aqil leave any house or property?' (Bukhari). In this hadith, the Prophet asked as a question: 'Did Aqil leave any piece of house or land for us where I can stay?' From this it is understood that the Prophet's land and house were taken by Aqil, who was a disbeliever at that time, and after possession, he became the owner. From this it is understood that if disbelievers take possession of our property, they become owners.

Imam Shafi'i says that disbelievers do not become owners of our property.

He says that the slave of Ibn Umar fled to the enemy and they took possession of him, then the Muslims overcame them, so the Prophet returned the slave to Ibn Umar and did not divide him among the Muslims. From this it is understood that even in dar al-harb, the slave remained the property of Ibn Umar; the harbi did not become its owner. The hadith: 'A slave of Ibn Umar fled to the enemy, then the Muslims overcame him, and the Messenger of Allah returned him to Ibn Umar and did not divide him' (Abu Dawud, Bukhari). In this hadith, the slave of Ibn Umar was returned, from which it is understood that the harbi did not become its owner. Ihraz: to collect, to take property from one country to another.

lent

(3020 (31) If Muslims overcome them and find it before division, it is for them without any compensation, and if they find it after division, they take it with price if they wish.

The harbi had captured our property; then the Muslims attacked and recovered the property. So if the owner finds the property before division, he will take it and will not give anything in exchange. And if division has occurred, then he gives the price to the one in whose hands it has gone and takes his property. And if he does not wish to take it by paying the price, he may not.

Before division, the booty is the property of the state; no mujahid has ownership. Therefore, there is no harm in taking it without any price. Since it was his property previously, it will be given to him. The hadith above is proof: From Ibn Umar that a slave of Ibn Umar fled to the enemy, then Muslims overcame him, and the Messenger of Allah returned him to Ibn Umar and did not divide it (Abu Dawud, Bukhari). In this hadith, the owner found the property before division, so it was returned to the owner.

And if division has occurred, then he takes from the owner with price. Its proof is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'Whatever the enemy captures and then the Muslims rescue from them, or its owner takes it before division, he is more entitled. And if he finds it after division, he may take it with price if he wishes' (Dar Qutni). From this hadith it is understood that if division has occurred, he returns with price.

Footnotes: (a) Allah has made the property of the townspeople His and the Messenger's... (b) Eat the booty, lawful and good... (c) For the poor emigrants... (d) Usama ibn Zayd asked: O Messenger of Allah, where will you alight in your house in Mecca? He replied: Did Aqil leave any land or house?

Footnotes: (a) A slave of Ibn Umar fled to the enemy, then Muslims captured him, and the Messenger returned him to Ibn Umar and did not divide. (b) A slave of Ibn Umar fled to the enemy, then Muslims captured him, and the Messenger returned him to Ibn Umar and did not divide. (c) He said: Whatever the enemy captures and then the Muslims rescue from them, or its owner takes it before division, he is more entitled. And if he finds it after division, he may take it with price.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Siyar of Al-Sharh al-Thamiri deals with the legal status of property captured by the enemy (harbi) from Muslims. The Hanafi position is that when the enemy takes Muslim property into dar al-harb (the abode of war), they become the legal owners of that property. This is established by the Quranic verses (Surah al-Hashr 59:7 and Surah al-Anfal 8:69) which describe captured property as 'booty' (ghanimah) and permit Muslims to consume it, implying ownership upon possession. The Prophet's practice of dividing the land of Khaybar among the mujahideen further supports this. Additionally, the hadith of Usama ibn Zayd indicates that the enemy's possession extinguishes the original owner's right, as the Prophet asked about Aqil's possession of his property.

Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that enemy possession does not transfer ownership. He cites the hadith of Ibn Umar's slave: the slave fled to the enemy, was recovered by Muslims, and the Prophet returned him to Ibn Umar without dividing him as booty. This suggests the slave remained Ibn Umar's property even after enemy capture. The Hanafi response, implicit in the following ruling (41), is that the slave was recovered before division of booty occurred; hence it was returned to its owner without compensation. This does not negate the enemy's ownership at the time of capture; rather, the rescue before division restores the original owner's right. The passage then details the practical consequences: if recovered before division, the property is returned to the original owner without payment; if after division, he must pay the current holder its value. The hadith of Ibn Abbas from Dar Qutni explicitly supports this distinction. Thus the Hanafi position is that enemy ownership is real but can be reversed by rescue under specific conditions.

Key Terms
احراز (ihraz): The act of taking possession and transporting property into dar al-harb, which according to Hanafi transfers ownership to the enemy.
غلبہ (ghalabah): Overcoming or military conquest, used here to describe the enemy's capture of Muslim property.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): The abode of war, i.e., enemy territory where Islamic law is not implemented.
غنیمت (ghanimah): Booty or spoils of war taken from the enemy.
فقراء (fuqara): Poor; in the Quranic verse, it refers to the Muhajirun who lost their property to the disbelievers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim finds his property that was captured by the enemy after it has been divided among the Muslim fighters, what must he do?
A) Take it without payment.
B) Pay the current holder its value.
C) Leave it as booty.
D) Ask for compensation from the state.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that enemy capture and transport to dar al-harb transfers ownership, but the original owner can reclaim without compensation before division or with payment after division.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Ownership of an Escaped Slave Recaptured from Harbis
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership of absconding Muslim slave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding harbi ownership of an escaped Muslim slave and evaluate the proofs cited by each side.

Core Idea
A slave escaping dar al-Islam becomes self-owned; harbis cannot own him like a free person.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of a Muslim slave who flees to enemy territory and is captured. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the harbis do not acquire ownership, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue they do. We will analyse the proofs from athars and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and each Imam's position
Locate the sentence stating the difference: 'Wala yamlikuhu 'inda Abi Hanifah wa qala malkuhu.' The two positions are clear.
Abu Hanifa: no ownership; Sahibayn: ownership.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that upon leaving dar al-Islam, the slave becomes self-owned, akin to a free person. Since harbis cannot own a free person, they cannot own the slave.
Key premise: the slave's legal status changes upon crossing the border.
3
Understand Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn analogize the slave to ordinary property: harbis acquire ownership of any property they seize. The same applies to the slave.
They treat the slave as a commodity, not as a person with potential self-ownership.
4
Trace the evidence for each side
Both sides cite the same athar from 'Umar but interpret it differently. Abu Hanifa focuses on the 'before division' clause; the Sahibayn focus on the 'after division' clause. An additional athar from 'Ali is used by the Sahibayn to support property status.
Understanding the different interpretations is key to grasping the ikhtilaf.

واذا ابق عبد المسلم فدخل اليهم فاخذوه لم يملكوه عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى وقالا ملكوه [۳۰۲۳ (۴۴) إذا مسلم كا غلام بھاگ جائے اور دار الحرب میں داخل ہو جائے اور وہ اس کو پکڑ لیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کا مالک نہیں بنیں گے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کا مالک بن جائیں گے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب غلام دارالاسلام میں سے نکلا تو اب وہ خود اپنی ذات کا مالک بن گیا اس لئے وہ اب آزاد کی طرح ہو گیا۔ اور آزاد کا حربی مالک نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح غلام کا بھی مالک نہیں ہو گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ كتب الى عمر بن الخطاب في عبد اسره المشركون ثم ظهر عليه المسلمون بعد ذلك قال صاحبه احق به مالم يقسم فاذا قسم مضى (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۳۰۰ في العبد ياسره المسلمون ثم ظهر عليه العدو، ج سادس، ص ۵۱۰، نمبر ۳۳۳۴۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تقسیم سے پہلے مالک کو دے دیا جائے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی اس کا ماک نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حربی غلام کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ وہ مال کے درجے میں ہے اور مال پر حربی کا قبضہ ہو جاتا ہے تو وہ مالک ہو جاتا ہے اسی طرح مسلمان کے غلام پر غلبہ ہو جائے گا تو وہ اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا (۲) اوپر کے اثر میں ہے کہ اگر غلام پر مسلمانوں کا دوبارہ قبضہ ہو گیا اور وہ تقسیم بھی ہو گیا تو جس کے حصے میں گیا وہ مجاہد اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی اس کا مالک ہو چکا تھا تب ہی تو حربی کے مال پر قبضے کے بعد مسلمان اس کا مالک بن گیا (۳) اثر میں ہے۔ عن قتادة قال على هو للمسلمين عامة لانه كان لهم مالا ( الف ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبة - ۳۰ في العبد ياسره المسلمون ثم ظهر عليه العدو، ج سادس ص ۵۱۰، نمبر ۳۳۳۴۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ وہ غلام حربی کا مال بن گیا اس لئے اس پر مسلمانوں کا قبضہ ہوا تو تمام مسلمانوں کا مال غنیمت ہوگا۔ ابق : بھاگ گیا۔
And if a Muslim's slave absconds and enters into them and they seize him, they do not own him according to Abu Hanifa - may Allah have mercy on him - and the two said they own him. [3023 (44)] If a Muslim's slave escapes and enters dar al-harb and they seize him, according to Abu Hanifa they will not become his owner. And the two companions say they will become his owner. Imam Abu Hanifa says: When the slave left dar al-Islam, he became the owner of his own self, so he became like a free man. And a free man is not owned by a harbi, similarly the slave will not be owned. (2) There is an indication in an athar: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab wrote regarding a slave captured by polytheists, then Muslims overcame them afterward: his owner has more right to him as long as he is not divided; if divided, it is passed.' (al-Musanaf of Ibn Abi Shaybah, 300, on the slave captured by Muslims then overtaken by the enemy, vol. 6, p. 510, no. 33340) In this athar, before division, the owner is given, from which it is understood that the harbi does not become owner. And the two companions say the harbi becomes owner of the slave. He is in the category of property, and a harbi gains ownership by seizure of property; similarly, if he overcomes a Muslim's slave, he becomes owner. (2) In the above athar, if Muslims regain possession of the slave and division occurs, the fighter in whose share he falls becomes owner. This indicates that the harbi had become owner, because only after the harbi's possession did the Muslim become owner upon seizing the harbi's property. (3) There is an athar from Qatada: 'Ali said, it is for the Muslims generally because it was their property' (Ibn Abi Shaybah, 30, on the slave captured by Muslims then overtaken, vol. 6, p. 510, no. 33342) In this athar, that slave became property of the harbi, so when Muslims seized it, it became booty for all Muslims. 'Abaqa' means he escaped.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the status of a Muslim slave who escapes to dar al-harb and is captured by harbis (enemy combatants). The text first states the positions: according to Abu Hanifa, the harbis do not acquire ownership of the slave; according to the Sahibayn, they do. The commentary then elaborates Abu Hanifa's reasoning: when the slave leaves dar al-Islam, he effectively gains self-ownership (like a free person), and since a free person cannot be owned by harbis, the slave likewise cannot be owned. This is supported by an athar from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab indicating that if Muslims recapture the slave before division, the original owner has priority, implying the harbi never acquired ownership. The Sahibayn, on the other hand, analogize the slave to ordinary property: since harbis gain ownership of property they seize, they also own the slave. They cite the same athar to argue that if the slave is divided among Muslims after recapture, the Muslim fighter becomes owner, which proves the harbi had owned him beforehand. Another athar from 'Ali is quoted suggesting that property taken from harbis becomes booty for all Muslims. The commentary follows the author's order: statement of the dispute, then each party's proof. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated in this passage, but in Hanafi fiqh, Abu Hanifa's view is often preferred in such matters.

Key Terms
أبق (abaqa): To abscond or escape (of a slave).
حربي (harbi): An enemy combatant or resident of dar al-harb with whom Muslims are in armed conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the athar from 'Umar cited in the passage, what is the ruling if the escaped slave is recaptured by Muslims before division of booty?
A) The slave becomes part of the booty for all Muslims.
B) The original owner has more right to the slave.
C) The slave is set free.
D) The harbis retain ownership.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school differs on whether an escaped slave becomes self-owned, with Abu Hanifa denying harbi ownership and the Sahibayn affirming it; the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

Ruling on a Camel Bolting to Harbis
Ruling that harbis own a camel that bolts to them during war.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a Muslim's camel bolts to harbis during war and explain why it differs from the slave case.

Core Idea
A camel that bolts to harbis becomes their property because it is pure property, unlike a slave who can escape.

In the previous lesson, we learned that a slave who bolts to the enemy and is captured does not become their property because a slave has intellect and can escape. This lesson examines a contrasting case: a camel, which is pure property. If a camel belonging to a Muslim bolts to the enemy lines during battle and they seize it, the harbis acquire ownership. This ruling follows the general principle that enemy capture of movable property transfers ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a camel (or any riding animal) bolting to harbis during battle, and the harbis seizing it. The ruling is that the harbis own it.
2
Understand the legal basis
Animals are classified as pure property in Hanafi fiqh. Unlike slaves, they have no intellect or agency, so their seizure by the enemy transfers ownership immediately.
3
Distinguish from the slave case
Previously, a slave who bolts to harbis is not owned by them because the slave can potentially escape or return. For property, capture equals ownership.
4
Confirm no conditions or exceptions
The ruling is unconditional: as long as the camel bolts to them and they seize it, ownership transfers. No further conditions (like the camel being a war commodity) are required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان نداليهم بعير فاخذوه ملكوه [۳۰۲۴) (۴۵) اگر کوئی اونٹ برک کر ان کی طرف چلا جائے اور وہ اس کو پکڑ لیں تو وہ مالک ہو جائیں گے۔ رہی چلا وہ اسکا ہو جنگ چل رہی تھی ایسی حالت میں اونٹ بلک کر اس کی طرف چلا گیا تو وہ اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔
And if a camel bolts to them and they seize it, they own it. [3024 (45)] If a camel bolts and goes towards them and they seize it, they become its owners. The commentary: it is property; it ran to them during battle; such a camel, if it bolts to them, they become its owners.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: if a camel (or any riding animal) belonging to Muslims bolts to the enemy lines during battle and the enemy seizes it, they acquire ownership of it. Unlike the previous case of a slave, a camel is pure property, and harbis gain ownership of property they physically capture. The commentary simply confirms the ruling without further proof, as it follows the general principle that enemy seizure of movable property transfers ownership.

Key Terms
ند (nadda): To bolt or run away (of an animal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The harbis own it because it is property
C) The camel remains the property of the original owner until the war ends
D) The imam decides its fate

Key Takeaway
Harbis acquire ownership of bolted camels because animals are property, unlike slaves who can escape.

Temporary Trust Distribution of Booty for Transport
Ruling that imam may distribute booty as trust for transport to dar al-Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on distributing booty as a trust (qismat iida') when the imam lacks transport, and cite the supporting evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
When the imam lacks transport, booty may be temporarily entrusted to fighters to carry to dar al-Islam for final division.

This passage addresses a practical problem in early Islamic warfare: how to transport booty from the battlefield (dar al-harb) to dar al-Islam when the imam does not have enough animals. The Hanafi school, following Imam Abu Hanifa, insists that the actual division of ownership must take place in dar al-Islam. Therefore, a temporary trust distribution is permitted to enable the fighters themselves to carry the booty. The proof is taken from the Prophet's practice at Ji'ranah after the Battle of Hunayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the temporary distribution of booty by the imam to the fighters for transport. The ruling is that it is permissible (sunnah) as a trust (qismat iida'), not a final division.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari that the Prophet performed Umrah from Ji'ranah where he divided the spoils of Hunayn. This implies the fighters themselves brought the booty there.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith support the ruling? The fact that the Prophet divided the booty at Ji'ranah—a location in dar al-Islam—indicates that division must occur there. That the fighters brought it themselves shows that temporary possession for transport is allowed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools permit division of booty in dar al-harb. The Hanafi school restricts division to dar al-Islam, which necessitates this trust mechanism when transport is lacking.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that booty is like a trust until properly divided, and the Prophet's practice at Ji'ranah is taken as a model. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(Urdu commentary follows) إذا امام کے پاس اتنے جانور نہ ہوں جن پر مال غنیمت لادے تو اس کو مجاہدین کے درمیان تقسیم کر دے امانت کی تقسیم تا کہ اس کو دارالاسلام لے آئیں۔ پھر ان سے واپس لے لے اور اس کو تقسیم کر دے۔ امام کے پاس اتنے جانور نہیں ہیں کہ ان پر سارا مال غنیمت لاد کر دار الاسلام لا سکے۔ ایسی صورت میں مال غنیمت امانت کے طور پر تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے مجاہدین کو دیدے تا کہ وہ اپنے جانوروں پر لاد کر دار الاسلام تک لائے ۔ جب دار الاسلام لے آئے تو امام سب مال کو جمع کرے اور ہر مجاہد کو اس کے حصے کے مطابق تقسیم کر کے دے اور مالک بنادے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک غنیمت دار الاسلام میں تقسیم کرنا ہے۔ اور دار الاسلام تک لانے کے لئے جانور میسر نہیں ہے تو یہی صورت ہو سکتی ہے کہ مجاہدین کو تھوڑا تھوڑا کر کے لانے کے لئے کہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے حسنین کی نعیمت جعرانہ میں تقسیم کی تو جعرانہ تک مجاہدین ہی، ال غنیمت لائے ہوں گے ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مجاہدین کو مال غنیمت لانے کے لئے دے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ ان انسا اخبـره قـال اعتمر النبي الله من الجعرانة حيث قسم غنائم حنين (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من قسم الغنيمة في غزوه و سفره ، ص ۱۴۳۱، نمبر ۳۰۶۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنگ حنین کی غنیمت جعرانہ میں تقسیم کی۔
3025 (46) And if the imam does not have transport to carry the booty, he divides it among the fighters as a trust division so that they carry it to dar al-Islam, then he takes it back from them and divides it. 3026 (47) And it is not permissible to sell booty before division in dar al-harb. (Urdu): If the imam does not have enough animals to load the booty, he distributes it among the fighters as a trust distribution so that they bring it to dar al-Islam. Then he takes it back from them and distributes it. According to Abu Hanifa, booty is to be divided in dar al-Islam. If there are no animals to bring it, this is the procedure: he asks the fighters to carry it bit by bit. (2) There is a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) divided the spoils of Hunayn at Ji'ranah, and the fighters themselves brought the booty to Ji'ranah. This indicates that the fighters are given the booty to bring. The hadith: Anas informed him saying: The Prophet performed Umrah from Ji'ranah where he divided the spoils of Hunayn. (Bukhari, Chapter on dividing booty in battle and travel, p. 1431, no. 3066) This hadith states that the spoils of Hunayn were divided at Ji'ranah.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage addresses the procedure for transporting booty from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam when the imam lacks sufficient transport animals. According to Abu Hanifa, the actual division of booty must take place in dar al-Islam. Therefore, if there is no transport, the imam may distribute the booty to the fighters as an amanah (trust) for the purpose of carriage. Each fighter carries a portion on his own animal to dar al-Islam, then returns it to the imam, who then performs the actual division and gives each fighter his rightful share. The evidence cited is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) dividing the spoils of Hunayn at Ji'ranah, which was a location near Mecca but considered dar al-Islam. The fact that the fighters carried the booty themselves demonstrates that such temporary distribution for transport is permissible.

Key Terms
قسمة ايداع (qismat iida'): Temporary distribution of booty as a trust for the purpose of transport.
جعرانة (al-Ji'ranah): A location near Mecca where the Prophet divided the spoils of Hunayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the imam distribute booty as a trust (qismat iida') to the fighters?
A) To reward them immediately for their efforts
B) Because the imam lacks animals to carry the booty to dar al-Islam
C) Because the booty must be divided only in dar al-Islam
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Booty must be divided in dar al-Islam; temporary distribution as trust for transport is permitted when the imam lacks the means to carry it.
